Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
Types of Divorce: Ahsan and Sunnah with Proofs
Defines two recommended divorce methods with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ahsan and sunnah methods of divorce, explain the proofs from Quran and hadith, and identify the conditions for a valid sunnah divorce.

Core Idea
The best divorce is one pronouncement in purity; Sunnah divorce is three over three pure periods.

This passage opens the Hanafi discussion on divorce. The author describes the two recommended methods and supports them with textual evidence. Understanding these methods helps distinguish between legitimate divorce practices and innovations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two methods described
Locate the definitions of ahsan and sunnah divorce. Note the key conditions: one vs three pronouncements, purity, and lack of intercourse.
Ahsan is a single irrevocable divorce; sunnah is three revocable pronouncements over three tuhr periods.
2
Extract the Quranic proofs
Two verses are cited: 65:1 commands divorce in the waiting period, and 2:229 states divorce is twice, then retention or release.
These verses establish that divorce must be done in a state where the waiting period can be counted.
3
Examine the hadith proof
A hadith from Ibn Umar declares divorce the most disliked permissible act, indicating its permissibility despite dislike.
This hadith is cited as a proof that divorce is halal, not as a direct proof for the methods.
4
Consider the salaf statements
Sayings of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i (tabi'i) and Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (companion) reinforce the recommended practice.
These statements provide early precedent for the sunnah method.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Hanafi school considers triple divorce in one sitting as bid'ah, while the Shafi'i school allows it as valid but disliked.
This difference arises from interpreting the Quranic 'divorce is twice' as a limit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الطَّلَاقِ
قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللهُ الطَّلَاقُ عَلَى ثَلَاثَةِ أَوْجُهِ لـ فَأَحْسَنُ الطَّلَاقِ أَنْ لَا يُطَلَّقَ امْرَأَتَهُ تَطْلِيقَةً وَاحِدَةً فِي طُهْرٍ لَمْ يُجَامِعْهَا فِيهِ وَيَتْرُكُهَا حَتَّى تَنْقَضِيَ عِدَّتُهَا ٣ وَطَلَاقُ السُّنَّةِ أَنْ يُطَلَّقَ الْمَدْخُولَ بِمَا ثَلَاثًا فِي ثَلَاثَةِ أَطْهَارٍ
لوجه: (1) الآية لثبوت الطَّلَاقُ عَلَى ثَلَاثَةِ أَوْجُهِ ا ﴿يَتأَيُّهَا النَّبِيُّ إِذَا طَلَّقْتُمُ النِّسَاءَ فَطَلِقُوهُنَّ لِعِدَّتِهِنَّ وَأَحْصُواْ الْعِدَّةَ ﴾ (القرآن،سورة الطلاق 65،الآية، نمبر 1)
وجه: (ا) الأية لثبوت الطَّلَاقُ عَلَى ثَلَاثَةِ أَوْجُهِ الطَّلَقُ مَرَّتَانِ فَإِمْسَاكُ بِمَعْرُوفٍ أَوْ تَسْرِيحُ بِإِحْسَنِ وَلَا يَحِلُّ لَكُمْ أَن تَأْخُذُوا مِمَّا ءَاتَيْتُمُوهُنَّ شَيْئًا إِلَّا أَن يَخَافًا أَلَّا يُقِيمَا حُدُودَ اللَّهِ ﴾ (القرآن، سورة البقرة2، الآية، نمبر 229)
وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت الطَّلَاقُ عَلَى ثَلَاثَةِ أَوْجُهِ \ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «أَبْغَضُ الْحَلَالِ إِلَى اللهِ عز وجل الطَّلَاقُ.» (سنن ابي داؤد شريف: باب في كراهية الطلاق،نمبر2178)
وجه : (۳)قول التابعى لثبوت الطَّلَاقُ عَلَى ثَلَاثَةِ أَوْجُهِ \ عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ قَالَ: «كَانُوا يَسْتَحِبُّونَ أَنْ يُطَلَّقَهَا وَاحِدَةً، ثُمَّ يَتْرُكَهَا حَتَّى تَحِيضَ ثَلَاثَ حِيَضِ» (مصنف ابن شيبه: ما يستحب من طلاق السنة، وكيف هو؟، نمبر 17743 )
وجه (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت فَأَحْسَنُ الطَّلَاقِ أَنْ لَا يُطَلِقَ امْرَأَتَهُ أَعَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ قَالَ: «مَنْ أَرَادَ الطَّلَاقَ الَّذِي هُوَ الطَّلَاقُ فَلْيُطَلِقْهَا تَطْلِيقَةً، ثُمَّ يَدَعَهَا حَتَّى تَحِيضَ ثَلَاثَ حِيْضِ» (مصنف ابن شيبه: ما يستحب من طلاق السنة وكيف هو؟، نمبر 17739 )
وجه : (۱)قول الصحابي لثبوت وَطَلَاقُ السُّنَّةِ أَنْ يُطَلَّقَ الْمَدْخُولَ بِمَا ثَلَاثًا \ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ أَنَّهُ قَالَ: «طَلَاقُ السُّنَّةِ تَطْلِيقَةٌ وَهِيَ طَاهِرٌ فِي غَيْرِ جِمَاعٍ، فَإِذَا حَاضَتْ وَطَهُرَتْ، طَلَّقَهَا أُخْرَى، فَإِذَا حَاضَتْ وَطَهُرَتْ طَلَّقَهَا أُخْرَى، ثُمَّ تَعْتَدُّ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ بِخَيْضَةٍ (سنن نسائي شريف: (۲) باب: طلاق السنة، نمبر3394)
اصول: عورت کو نکاح سے الگ کرنے کو طلاق کہتے ہیں ، اور اگرچہ طلاق عند اللہ حلال اشیاء میں سب سے زیادہ ناپسندیدہ ہے لیکن قرآن و حدیث سے اس کا ثبوت ملتا ہے۔
Book of Divorce. He (the author, may Allah have mercy on him) said: Divorce is of three types: The best divorce is that he should not divorce his wife more than one pronouncement in a state of purity during which he has not had intercourse with her, and he leaves her until her waiting period expires. And the Sunnah divorce is that he divorces the wife with whom he has consummated marriage three times in three pure periods. Proof (1): The verse for establishing that divorce is of three types: 'O Prophet, when you divorce women, divorce them for their waiting period and count the waiting period' (Quran 65:1). Proof (a): The verse for establishing that divorce is of three types: 'Divorce is twice; then either hold her in kindness or let her go with kindness' (Quran 2:229). Proof (2): The hadith for establishing that divorce is of three types: On the authority of Ibn 'Umar from the Prophet (peace be upon him) who said: 'The most hateful of permissible things to Allah is divorce.' (Abu Dawud no. 2178). Proof (3): The saying of the tabi'i for establishing that divorce is of three types: On the authority of Ibrahim who said: 'They used to recommend that he divorce her once, then leave her until she menstruates three times' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah no. 17743). Proof (1): The saying of the Companion for establishing the best divorce: On the authority of 'Abdullah (Ibn Mas'ud) who said: 'Whoever wants the divorce that is truly divorce, let him divorce her one pronouncement, then leave her until she menstruates three times' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah no. 17739). Proof (1): The saying of the Companion for establishing Sunnah divorce: On the authority of 'Abdullah that he said: 'Sunnah divorce is one pronouncement while she is pure without intercourse; then when she menstruates and becomes pure, he gives her another; then when she menstruates and becomes pure, he gives her another; then she observes her waiting period after that with one menstruation' (Nasa'i no. 3394). Principle: Separating a woman from marriage is called talaq, and although divorce is the most disliked of permissible things to Allah, its legitimacy is established from the Quran and hadith.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage from the Quduri text opens the Book of Divorce. The author states that divorce is of three types, but then describes two: the best (ahsan) and the Sunnah. The best divorce is a single pronouncement in a clean state (tuhr) without intercourse, after which the husband leaves the wife to complete her waiting period (iddah) without taking her back. This is called the 'ahsan' (best) method. The Sunnah divorce consists of one pronouncement in each clean period (tuhr) for three consecutive clean periods, totaling three pronouncements over three months. The text then provides proofs from the Quran (65:1 and 2:229) which indicate that divorce is to be done in the waiting period and that divorce is twice (allowing revocation) followed by either retention or release. A hadith from Ibn 'Umar declares divorce the most disliked permissible act. Statements from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i (a tabi'i) and Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (a companion) further elaborate the recommended practice. The Urdu principle at the end defines talaq linguistically and reminds that despite its dislike, it is legislated.

Key Terms
الطلاق (aṭ-ṭalāq): The dissolution of a marriage contract by the husband's pronouncement.
أحسن الطلاق (aḥsan aṭ-ṭalāq): The best divorce: one pronouncement in a state of purity without intercourse, then leaving her until the iddah ends.
طلاق السنة (ṭalāq as-sunnah): The Sunnah divorce: one pronouncement in each of three pure states, totaling three divorces over three periods.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the 'ahsan' (best) method of divorce according to the Quduri text?
A) Three divorces in one sitting
B) One pronouncement in a state of purity without intercourse, then leaving her until iddah ends
C) Three pronouncements in three separate pure states
D) One pronouncement during menstruation

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school teaches that divorce should be performed in one of two sunnah methods, with ahsan being a single pronouncement in purity, as supported by Quran and hadith.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate

The Three Types of Divorce: Hasan, Sunnah, and Bid'ah
Defines three types of divorce with proofs from Quran, Sunnah, and Companions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three types of divorce in Hanafi fiqh, identify the ruling for each, and explain why bid'ah divorce is effective despite being sinful.

Core Idea
Divorce has three types: two sunnah (ahsan and sunnah) and one bid'ah; all are legally effective, but bid'ah is sinful.

Divorce (talaq) is a permissible act but intensely disliked by Allah. The Hanafi school classifies the methods of divorce into three categories: the best (ahsan), the proper sunnah, and the innovated (bid'ah). This lesson unpacks these categories, their conditions, and their legal effects, drawing on the proofs cited by Imam al-Quduri in his matn. Understanding this classification is essential for correctly applying divorce law and avoiding common errors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types and their definitions
Read the opening definitions. The 'hasan' divorce is one divorce in a pure state without intercourse, followed by waiting until 'iddah ends. The 'sunnah' divorce is three divorces in three separate periods of purity for a consummated marriage. The 'bid'ah' divorce is any departure from these, e.g., three divorces in one utterance or in one purity period.
Memorize the conditions for each type.
2
Understand the legal effect of bid'ah divorce
The text states that if a man performs a bid'ah divorce, the divorce occurs, she becomes irrevocably separated (ba'in), and he is sinful. This establishes that bid'ah divorce is legally effective despite being prohibited.
This is a key Hanafi rule: sinfulness does not invalidate the act.
3
Analyze the proofs (dalil) cited
The text provides ten proofs from Quran, hadith, and sayings of Companions and tabi'een. Locate the primary Quranic verses (65:1, 2:229) and the hadith about triple talaq causing the Prophet's anger. Note how each proof supports the classification.
Focus on the hadith of Mahmud ibn Labid and Ibn 'Umar as primary evidence for sunnah and bid'ah.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a husband who says 'You are divorced, divorced, divorced' in one sitting. According to the text, three divorces occur, she becomes ba'in, and he is sinful. This is the mufta bihi position of the Hanafi school.
Contrast with schools that count it as one divorce.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الطَّلَاقِ
قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللهُ - الطَّلَاقُ عَلَى ثَلَاثَةِ أَوْجُهٍ: فَأَحْسَنُ الطَّلَاقِ أَنْ لَا يُطَلِّقَ امْرَأَتَهُ تَطْلِيقَةً وَاحِدَةً فِي طُهْرٍ لَمْ يُجَامِعْهَا فِيهِ، وَيَتْرُكَهَا حَتَّى تَنْقَضِيَ عِدَّتُهَا. وَطَلَاقُ السُّنَّةِ أَنْ يُطَلِّقَ الْمَدْخُولَ بِهَا ثَلَاثًا فِي ثَلَاثَةِ أَطْهَارٍ. وَطَلَاقُ الْبِدْعَةِ أَنْ يُطَلِّقَهَا ثَلَاثًا بِكَلِمَةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ أَوْ ثَلَاثًا فِي طُهْرٍ وَاحِدٍ. فَإِذَا فَعَلَ ذَلِكَ وَقَعَ الطَّلَاقُ وَبَانَتْ مِنْهُ وَكَانَ عَاصِيًا.

الْأَدِلَّةُ:
وَجْهٌ (١) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ الطَّلَاقِ عَلَى ثَلَاثَةِ أَوْجُهٍ: {يَا أَيُّهَا النَّبِيُّ إِذَا طَلَّقْتُمُ النِّسَاءَ فَطَلِّقُوهُنَّ لِعِدَّتِهِنَّ وَأَحْصُوا الْعِدَّةَ} (الطلاق: ١).
وَجْهٌ (٢) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ الطَّلَاقِ عَلَى ثَلَاثَةِ أَوْجُهٍ: {الطَّلَاقُ مَرَّتَانِ فَإِمْسَاكٌ بِمَعْرُوفٍ أَوْ تَسْرِيحٌ بِإِحْسَانٍ} (البقرة: ٢٢٩).
وَجْهٌ (٣) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ الطَّلَاقِ عَلَى ثَلَاثَةِ أَوْجُهٍ: عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «أَبْغَضُ الْحَلَالِ إِلَى اللهِ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ الطَّلَاقُ». (سنن أبي داود، باب في كراهية الطلاق، رقم ٢١٧٨).
وَجْهٌ (٤) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ الطَّلَاقِ عَلَى ثَلَاثَةِ أَوْجُهٍ: عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ قَالَ: «كَانُوا يَسْتَحِبُّونَ أَنْ يُطَلِّقَهَا وَاحِدَةً، ثُمَّ يَتْرُكَهَا حَتَّى تَحِيضَ ثَلَاثَ حِيَضٍ». (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة، ما يستحب من طلاق السنة، رقم ١٧٧٤٣).
وَجْهٌ (٥) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ فَأَحْسَنُ الطَّلَاقِ: عَنْ عَبْدِ اللهِ قَالَ: «مَنْ أَرَادَ الطَّلَاقَ الَّذِي هُوَ الطَّلَاقُ فَلْيُطَلِّقْهَا تَطْلِيقَةً، ثُمَّ يَدَعَهَا حَتَّى تَحِيضَ ثَلَاثَ حِيَضٍ». (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة، ما يستحب من طلاق السنة، رقم ١٧٧٣٩).
وَجْهٌ (٦) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ طَلَاقِ السُّنَّةِ: عَنْ عَبْدِ اللهِ أَنَّهُ قَالَ: «طَلَاقُ السُّنَّةِ تَطْلِيقَةٌ وَهِيَ طَاهِرٌ فِي غَيْرِ جِمَاعٍ، فَإِذَا حَاضَتْ وَطَهُرَتْ، طَلَّقَهَا أُخْرَى، فَإِذَا حَاضَتْ وَطَهُرَتْ طَلَّقَهَا أُخْرَى، ثُمَّ تَعْتَدُّ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ بِحَيْضَةٍ». (سنن النسائي، باب طلاق السنة، رقم ٣٣٩٤).
وَجْهٌ (٧) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ طَلَاقِ السُّنَّةِ: عَنْ عَبْدِ اللهِ بْنِ عُمَرَ رضي الله عنهما «أَنَّهُ طَلَّقَ امْرَأَتَهُ وَهِيَ حَائِضٌ عَلَى عَهْدِ رَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَسَأَلَ عُمَرُ بْنُ الْخَطَّابِ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَنْ ذَلِكَ، فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: مُرْهُ فَلْيُرَاجِعْهَا، ثُمَّ لِيُمْسِكْهَا حَتَّى تَطْهُرَ، ثُمَّ تَحِيضَ ثُمَّ تَطْهُرَ، ثُمَّ إِنْ شَاءَ أَمْسَكَ بَعْدُ، وَإِنْ شَاءَ طَلَّقَ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَمَسَّ، فَتِلْكَ الْعِدَّةُ الَّتِي أَمَرَ اللهُ أَنْ تُطَلَّقَ لَهَا النِّسَاءُ». (صحيح البخاري، باب قول الله تعالى يا أيها النبي إذا طلقتم النساء فطلقوهن لعدتهن، رقم ٥٢٥١؛ صحيح مسلم، باب تحريم طلاق الحائض بغير رضاها، رقم ١٤٧١).
وَجْهٌ (٨) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ طَلَاقِ الْبِدْعَةِ: سَمِعْتُ مَحْمُودَ بْنَ لَبِيدٍ قَالَ: أُخْبِرَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَنْ رَجُلٍ طَلَّقَ امْرَأَتَهُ ثَلَاثَ تَطْلِيقَاتٍ جَمِيعًا، فَقَامَ غَضْبَانًا، ثُمَّ قَالَ: «أَيُلْعَبُ بِكِتَابِ اللهِ وَأَنَا بَيْنَ أَظْهُرِكُمْ». (سنن النسائي، طلاق الثلاث المجموعة، رقم ٥٥٦٤).
وَجْهٌ (٩) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ طَلَاقِ الْبِدْعَةِ: أَنَّ سَهْلَ بْنَ سَعْدٍ السَّاعِدِيَّ أَخْبَرَهُ أَنَّ عُوَيْمِرًا الْعَجْلَانِيَّ جَاءَ إِلَى عَاصِمٍ، قَالَ عُوَيْمِرٌ: كَذَبْتُ عَلَيْهَا يَا رَسُولَ اللهِ إِنْ أَمْسَكْتُهَا، فَطَلَّقَهَا ثَلَاثًا قَبْلَ أَنْ يَأْمُرَهُ رَسُولُ اللهِ. (صحيح البخاري، باب من أجاز طلاق الثلاث، رقم ٥٢٥٩؛ صحيح مسلم، كتاب اللعان، رقم ١٤٩٢).
وَجْهٌ (١٠) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ طَلَاقِ الْبِدْعَةِ: عَنْ مُجَاهِدٍ قَالَ: كُنْتُ عِنْدَ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ فَجَاءَهُ رَجُلٌ فَقَالَ: إِنَّهُ طَلَّقَ امْرَأَتَهُ ثَلَاثًا، قَالَ: فَسَكَتَ حَتَّى ظَنَنْتُ أَنَّهُ رَادُّهَا إِلَيْهِ، ثُمَّ قَالَ: يَنْطَلِقُ أَحَدُكُمْ فَيَرْكَبُ الْحَمُوقَةَ ثُمَّ يَقُولُ: يَا ابْنَ عَبَّاسٍ يَا ابْنَ عَبَّاسٍ، وَإِنَّ اللهَ قَالَ: {وَمَنْ يَتَّقِ اللهَ يَجْعَلْ لَهُ مَخْرَجًا}، وَإِنَّكَ لَمْ تَتَّقِ اللهَ فَلَا أَجِدُ لَكَ مَخْرَجًا، عَصَيْتَ رَبَّكَ وَبَانَتْ مِنْكَ امْرَأَتُكَ. (سنن أبي داود، باب نسخ المراجعة بعد التطليقات الثلاث، رقم ٢١٩٧؛ مصنف ابن أبي شيبة، من كره أن يطلق الرجل امرأته ثلاثا في مقعد واحد، رقم ١٧٧٨٩).

اصول: طلاق کی تین قسمیں ہیں: (١) طلاق احسن کہ بغیر وطی کے ایک طہر میں ایک طلاق دے۔ (٢) طلاق سنت: کہ مدخول بہا کو تین طہروں میں تین طلاق دے۔ (٣) طلاق بدعت: مذکورہ دونوں صورتوں کے برعکس۔
Book of Divorce. He (may God have mercy on him) said: Divorce is of three types: The best (hasan) divorce is that he does not divorce his wife except one divorce in a period of purity in which he has not had intercourse with her, and he leaves her until her waiting period expires. The sunnah divorce is that he divorces a wife who has been consummated with three times in three periods of purity. The bid'ah divorce is that he divorces her three times with one word or three times in one period of purity. If he does that, the divorce occurs, she becomes separated from him, and he is sinful. The proofs: (1) The verse for establishing divorce in three ways: {O Prophet, when you divorce women, divorce them for their waiting period and count the waiting period} (65:1). (2) The verse: {Divorce is twice, then either retention in kindness or release with goodness} (2:229). (3) The hadith: from Ibn 'Umar from the Prophet (PBUH) who said: "The most hateful of permissible things to God Almighty is divorce." (4) The saying of the tabi'i: from Ibrahim who said: "They used to prefer that he divorce her once, then leave her until she menstruates three times." (5) The saying of the Companion: from 'Abdullah who said: "Whoever intends divorce which is the [proper] divorce, let him divorce her once, then leave her until she menstruates three times." (6) The saying of the Companion regarding sunnah divorce: from 'Abdullah that he said: "Sunnah divorce is one divorce while she is pure without intercourse; when she menstruates and becomes pure, he divorces her again; when she menstruates and becomes pure, he divorces her again; then she observes her waiting period after that with one menstruation." (7) The hadith for sunnah divorce: from 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar (may God be pleased with both) that he divorced his wife while she was menstruating during the time of the Messenger of God (PBUH), so 'Umar ibn al-Khattab asked the Messenger of God about that, and the Messenger of God said: "Order him to take her back, then keep her until she becomes pure, then menstruates, then becomes pure; then if he wishes he may keep her, and if he wishes he may divorce before touching her; that is the waiting period which God has commanded that women be divorced for." (8) The hadith for bid'ah divorce: Mahmud ibn Labid said: The Messenger of God (PBUH) was informed about a man who divorced his wife three times all at once; he stood up angry, then said: "Is the Book of God being played with while I am among you?" (9) The hadith: that Sahl ibn Sa'd al-Sa'idi informed him that 'Uwaymir al-'Ajlani came to 'Asim; 'Uwaymir said: "I would be lying about her, O Messenger of God, if I kept her," so he divorced her three times before the Messenger of God ordered him. (10) The saying of the tabi'i: from Mujahid who said: I was with Ibn 'Abbas when a man came and said: He divorced his wife three times. He was silent until I thought he would return her to him, then he said: One of you goes and commits foolishness, then says: O Ibn 'Abbas, O Ibn 'Abbas! And God said: {And whoever fears God, He will make for him a way out}. You did not fear God, so I find no way out for you; you disobeyed your Lord, and your wife has become separated from you. Principles: Divorce is of three types: (1) Hasan divorce: to give one divorce in one purity without intercourse. (2) Sunnah divorce: to give three divorces in three purities to a wife who has been consummated. (3) Bid'ah divorce: the opposite of the above two forms.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage from al-Quduri's Kitab al-Talaq states the three types of divorce with their proofs. It opens by defining the three types: hasan (best), sunnah (proper), and bid'ah (innovated). The hasan divorce involves a single divorce in a period of purity without intercourse, after which the husband leaves her until her 'iddah ends. This is considered the best method because it allows maximum opportunity for reconciliation. The sunnah divorce is for a wife with whom intercourse has occurred; the husband gives three divorces over three distinct periods of purity, one each, following the prophetic practice. The bid'ah divorce is any departure from these methods, such as giving three divorces in one utterance or three times within a single purity period. Although such a divorce is sinful (the husband is 'asi), it is legally effective: the divorce occurs and she becomes irrevocably separated (ba'in). The text then provides extensive proofs from the Quran, hadith, and sayings of Companions and tabi'een. The Quranic verses from Surat al-Talaq (65:1) and Surat al-Baqarah (2:229) establish the permissibility and regulation of divorce. The hadith from Ibn 'Umar declaring divorce the most hated permissible thing underscores its gravity. The practice of the Companions and the later authorities defines the sunnah and hasan methods. The hadith of Mahmud ibn Labid and the incident of 'Uwaymir show that triple divorce in one sitting was considered a grave sin but was still enforced. The saying of Ibn 'Abbas indicates that such a man has no way out because he disobeyed God. The Urdu summary reiterates the three categories.

Key Terms
الطلاق (al-talaq): The dissolution of marriage by the husband's pronouncement.
الطلاق الأحسن (al-talaq al-ahsan): A single divorce in a state of purity without intercourse, followed by leaving her until 'iddah expires.
طلاق السنة (talaq al-sunnah): Three divorces given in three separate periods of purity for a consummated marriage.
طلاق البدعة (talaq al-bid'ah): Divorce contrary to sunnah, e.g., triple divorce in one utterance or during menstruation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a man divorces his wife three times in one utterance?
A) It is invalid and no divorce occurs.
B) Only one divorce occurs because it is bid'ah.
C) Three divorces occur, she becomes irrevocably separated, and he is sinful.
D) It is valid only if the wife agrees.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school classifies divorce into three types; the key legal point is that bid'ah divorce is effective (three divorces occur) despite being sinful.

10 min
Bid'ah Talaq: Its Definition and Proofs
Definition of bid'ah talaq with four proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of bid'ah talaq, identify its four proofs, and explain why it is valid but sinful in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Bid'ah talaq is sinful but effective: three divorces in one utterance count as three.

This passage from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar introduces the concept of bid'ah talaq—divorce that violates the sunnah. The author defines it as three divorces pronounced in a single utterance and then provides four proofs to establish that it is valid (waqi') yet sinful. Understanding this ruling is crucial for distinguishing between the legal effect and the moral status of an act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is bid'ah talaq (three divorces in one utterance). The ruling: it is haram (sinful) but legally effective (waqi').
The passage explicitly states 'the divorce occurs, but he sins.'
2
Locate the first proof (Quran)
Surah Al-Baqarah (2:230) implies that after three divorces, the wife is unlawful until she marries another. This supports that three divorces in one go are effective because the wife becomes unlawful after three.
Wajh al-dalalah: the verse ends finality after three.
3
Examine the second proof (hadith of 'Imran ibn Husayn)
The hadith states that the man 'sinned against his Lord and his wife was forbidden to him.' This confirms both the sinfulness and the effectiveness of the divorce.
The word 'sinned' (athima) shows haram, and 'forbidden' (hurrimat) shows validity.
4
Analyze the third proof (hadith of Ibn 'Abbas on 'Umar's practice)
During the Prophet's time and Abu Bakr's, three divorces were counted as one. 'Umar changed this to three due to people's haste, and the companions accepted. This shows the ruling's evolution and final enforcement.
'Umar's ijtihad is accepted as binding.
5
Consider the fourth proof (hadith of Ibn 'Umar)
The Prophet ordered Ibn 'Umar to take back his wife after divorcing her during menstruation. This indicates that the bid'ah divorce (due to timing) was valid, otherwise no reconciliation would have been needed.
The order to take back implies the divorce had occurred.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الطَّلَاقِ. وَطَلَاقُ الْبِدْعَةِ أَنْ يُطَلَّقَهَا ثَلَاثًا بِكَلِمَةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ. وَالدَّلِيلُ عَلَيْهِ: قَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى: {فَإِن طَلَّقَهَا فَلَا تَحِلُّ لَهُ مِن بَعْدُ حَتَّى تَنكِحَ زَوْجًا غَيْرَهُ} [البقرة: 230]. وَعَنْ عِمْرَانَ بْنِ حُصَيْنٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: «أَثِمَ بِرَبِّهِ وَحُرِّمَتْ عَلَيْهِ امْرَأَتُهُ». وَعَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا قَالَ: «كَانَ الطَّلَاقُ عَلَى عَهْدِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَأَبِي بَكْرٍ وَسَنَتَيْنِ مِنْ خِلَافَةِ عُمَرَ طَلَاقُ الثَّلَاثِ وَاحِدَةً، فَقَالَ عُمَرُ بْنُ الْخَطَّابِ: إِنَّ النَّاسَ قَدِ اسْتَعْجَلُوا فِي أَمْرٍ قَدْ كَانَتْ لَهُمْ فِيهِ أَنَاةٌ، فَلَوْ أَمْضَيْنَاهُ عَلَيْهِمْ فَأَمْضَاهُ عَلَيْهِمْ». وَعَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ أَيْضًا قَالَ: «وَأَمَّا الْحَرَامُ فَأَنْ يُطَلَّقَهَا وَهِيَ حَائِضٌ أَوْ يُطَلَّقَهَا حِينَ يُجَامِعُهَا لَا تَدْرِي أَشْتَمَلَ الرَّحِمُ عَلَى وَلَدٍ أَمْ لَا؟». وَعَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عُمَرَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا «أَنَّهُ طَلَّقَ امْرَأَتَهُ وَهِيَ حَائِضٌ فَذَكَرَ عُمَرُ لِلنَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَقَالَ: لِيُرَاجِعْهَا». وَقَالَ الْأُصُولِيُّونَ: إِذَا كَانَ طَلَاقٌ بِدْعِيًّا فَإِنَّهُ يَقَعُ الطَّلَاقُ وَلَكِنْ يَأْثَمُ.
Book of Divorce. And bid'ah divorce is that he divorces her three times with one word. And the proof for it: His statement Most High: {And if he divorces her, she is not lawful for him after that until she marries another husband} [Al-Baqarah 230]. And from 'Imran ibn Husayn may Allah be pleased with him, he said: 'He has sinned against his Lord, and his wife has been made forbidden to him.' And from Ibn 'Abbas may Allah be pleased with them both, he said: 'Divorce was on the era of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and Abu Bakr and two years of the Caliphate of 'Umar, divorce of three as one. So 'Umar ibn al-Khattab said: The people have hastened in a matter in which they had patience, so if we enforce it upon them? And he enforced it upon them.' And from Ibn 'Abbas also he said: 'As for the forbidden, it is that he divorces her while she is menstruating or he divorces her at the time he has intercourse with her, not knowing whether the womb has conceived a child or not.' And from 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar may Allah be pleased with them both, that he divorced his wife while she was menstruating, so 'Umar mentioned it to the Prophet (peace be upon him), and he said: 'Let him take her back.' And the usulis said: If it is a bid'ah divorce, then the divorce occurs, but he sins.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage defines bid'ah talaq as three divorces pronounced in a single sentence. It is called bid'ah because it violates the sunnah method of divorce, which requires one divorce per tuhr period. The author then provides four proofs: (1) The Quranic verse from Surah al-Baqarah (230) which implies that after three divorces, the wife becomes unlawful until she marries another, confirming that three divorces in one go are effective. (2) The hadith of 'Imran ibn Husayn stating that the man sins and his wife is forbidden, meaning the divorce takes effect. (3) The famous hadith of Ibn 'Abbas that during the time of the Prophet (SAW) and Abu Bakr and the early part of 'Umar's caliphate, three divorces were counted as one, but 'Umar changed the practice due to people's haste, making three divorces count as three. This shows that the ruling is effective. (4) The hadith of Ibn 'Umar where the Prophet ordered him to take back his wife, indicating that the divorce was valid, even though it was bid'ah due to being during her menses. The usul principle concludes that bid'ah divorce is valid but sinful.

Key Terms
طَلَاقُ الْبِدْعَةِ (talaq al-bid'ah): Divorce that violates the sunnah method, typically three divorces in one utterance or during menstruation.
وَقَعَ الطَّلَاقُ (waqa'a al-talaq): The divorce takes effect legally.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling of bid'ah talaq (three divorces in one utterance) in Hanafi fiqh?
A) It is invalid and no divorce occurs.
B) It is valid but sinful.
C) It is valid and recommended.
D) It is sinful and invalid.

Key Takeaway
Bid'ah talaq (three divorces in one utterance) is valid and counts as three, but the husband commits a sin by violating the sunnah.

The Sunnah Method of Divorce: Number and Timing
Ruling with proof on sunnah divorce aspects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah method of divorce for number and timing, and apply it to different categories of wives.

Core Idea
Sunnah talaq: one divorce per occasion, in a pure state without intercourse for consummated wives.

Divorce in Islam is permitted but disliked, and the Prophet ﷺ taught the best way to execute it. This passage from al-Quduri outlines the sunnah method in two dimensions: how many divorces to give and when. Understanding these rules protects Muslim families from regret and preserves the possibility of reconciliation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two aspects
The passage divides sunnah talaq into two aspects: number (al-'adad) and timing (al-waqt). Note which applies to all wives and which is specific.
Number applies to both consummated and unconsummated; timing only to consummated.
2
State the sunnah in number
For all wives, the sunnah is to give only one divorce at a time. The proof is the practice of the salaf as reported by Ibrahim al-Nakha'i.
Giving three divorces at once is bid'ah but valid (per Hanafi).
3
State the sunnah in timing for consummated wives
For al-madkhul biha, the husband must divorce her in a state of purity (tuhr) during which he has not had intercourse. The proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar.
This ensures no ambiguity about pregnancy and allows for reconciliation.
4
Apply to unconsummated and non-menstruating women
Unconsummated wives may be divorced at any time, even during menstruation, because they have no iddah. Non-menstruating women (due to youth or menopause) are divorced one divorce per month, based on Quran 65:4 and the practice of al-Zuhri.
Each month stands in place of a menstrual cycle for the purpose of timing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالسُّنَّةُ فِي الطَّلَاقِ مِنْ وَجْهَيْنِ: سُنَّةٌ فِي الْوَقْتِ وَسُنَّةٌ فِي الْعَدَدِ. فَالسُّنَّةُ فِي الْعَدَدِ يَسْتَوِي فِيهَا الْمَدْخُولُ بِهَا وَغَيْرُ الْمَدْخُولِ بِهَا، أَنْ يُطَلَّقَهَا وَاحِدَةً. وَالدَّلِيلُ: عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ النَّخَعِيِّ قَالَ: «كَانُوا يَسْتَحِبُّونَ أَنْ يُطَلَّقَهَا وَاحِدَةً، ثُمَّ يَتْرُكَهَا حَتَّى تَحِيضَ ثَلَاثَ حِيَضٍ». وَالسُّنَّةُ فِي الْوَقْتِ تَثْبُتُ فِي الْمَدْخُولِ بِهَا خَاصَّةً، وَهُوَ أَنْ يُطَلَّقَهَا فِي طُهْرٍ لَمْ يُجَامِعْهَا فِيهِ. وَالدَّلِيلُ: حَدِيثُ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عُمَرَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا أَنَّهُ طَلَّقَ امْرَأَتَهُ وَهِيَ حَائِضٌ، فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «لِيُرَاجِعْهَا ثُمَّ لِيُمْسِكْهَا حَتَّى تَطْهُرَ ثُمَّ تَحِيضَ ثُمَّ تَطْهُرَ، ثُمَّ إِنْ شَاءَ أَمْسَكَ بَعْدُ، وَإِنْ شَاءَ طَلَّقَ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَمَسَّ، فَتِلْكَ الْعِدَّةُ الَّتِي أَمَرَ اللَّهُ أَنْ تُطَلَّقَ لَهَا النِّسَاءُ». وَغَيْرُ الْمَدْخُولِ بِهَا يُطَلِّقُهَا فِي حَالَةِ الطُّهْرِ وَالْحَيْضِ. وَالدَّلِيلُ: عَنِ الثَّوْرِيِّ فِي رَجُلٍ طَلَّقَ الْبِكْرَ حَائِضًا قَالَ: «لَا بَأْسَ بِهِ لِأَنَّهُ لَا عِدَّةَ لَهَا». وَإِذَا كَانَتِ الْمَرْأَةُ لَا تَحِيضُ مِنْ صِغَرٍ أَوْ كِبَرٍ، وَأَرَادَ أَنْ يُطَلِّقَهَا لِلسُّنَّةِ، طَلَّقَهَا وَاحِدَةً مَتَى شَاءَ. وَالدَّلِيلُ: قَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى: {وَاللَّائِي يَئِسْنَ مِنَ الْمَحِيضِ مِن نِّسَائِكُمْ إِنِ ارْتَبْتُمْ فَعِدَّتُهُنَّ ثَلَاثَةُ أَشْهُرٍ} [الطلاق: 4]. وَعَنِ الزُّهْرِيِّ: فِي الْبِكْرِ الَّتِي لَمْ تَحِضْ وَالَّتِي قَعَدَتْ مِنَ الْحَيْضِ: «طَلَاقُهَا كُلَّ هِلَالٍ تَطْلِيقَةٌ». وَالْأَصْلُ: الْمَرْأَةُ الَّتِي لَا تَحِيضُ، يُعْتَبَرُ كُلُّ شَهْرٍ بِمَنْزِلَةِ حَيْضَةٍ.
And the sunnah in divorce is from two aspects: sunnah in timing and sunnah in number. As for the sunnah in number, it is equal regarding the one who has been consummated with and the one who has not been consummated with: that he divorces her once. And the proof: from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, he said: 'They used to recommend that he divorces her once, then leave her until she completes three menstrual cycles.' And the sunnah in timing is established specifically for the one who has been consummated with, and it is that he divorces her in a state of purity in which he has not had intercourse with her. And the proof: the hadith of Abdullah ibn Umar may Allah be pleased with them both, that he divorced his wife while she was menstruating, so the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Let him take her back, then let him keep her until she becomes pure, then menstruates, then becomes pure; then if he wishes, he may keep her after that, and if he wishes, he may divorce before touching her; that is the iddah which Allah has commanded that women be divorced for.' And the one who has not been consummated with, he may divorce her in a state of purity or menstruation. And the proof: from al-Thawri regarding a man who divorced a virgin while she was menstruating, he said: 'There is no harm in it because she has no iddah.' And if the woman does not menstruate due to young age or old age, and he wants to divorce her according to the sunnah, he divorces her once whenever he wishes. And the proof: His statement Most High: {And those who have despaired of menstruation from your women, if you are in doubt, their iddah is three months} [Al-Talaq: 4]. And from al-Zuhri regarding the virgin who has not menstruated and the one who has stopped menstruation: 'Her divorce is one divorce every month.' And the principle: the woman who does not menstruate, each month is considered in the position of a menstruation.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage explains the sunnah method of divorce in two aspects. First, the sunnah in number: for both consummated and unconsummated marriages, the sunnah is to give only one divorce at a time. This is supported by the practice of the salaf as reported by Ibrahim al-Nakha'i. Second, the sunnah in timing applies specifically to consummated marriages: the husband must wait for a state of purity (tuhr) during which he has not had intercourse and then pronounce one divorce. The hadith of Ibn Umar provides the detailed procedure. For unconsummated marriages, timing does not matter because there is no iddah, so divorce can be given even during menstruation. For women who do not menstruate (due to youth or old age), the sunnah is to give one divorce per month, based on the Quranic verse about iddah of three months. The principle is that each month is treated like a menstrual cycle for the purpose of spacing divorces.

Key Terms
السنة في العدد (al-sunnah fi al-'adad): The recommended number of divorces: one divorce at a time.
المدخول بها (al-madkhul biha): A wife with whom the husband has consummated the marriage.
الطهر (al-tuhr): State of purity between menstrual periods.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the sunnah in number when divorcing any wife?
A) Two divorces at once
B) One divorce at a time
C) Three divorces at once
D) One divorce during menstruation

Key Takeaway
The sunnah talaq requires one divorce at a time, with timing adjusted based on the wife's menstrual status.

6 min
Sunnah Divorce: Number and Time
Defines the two sunnah aspects of divorce and provides proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two sunnah aspects of divorce and apply the ruling to both consummated and non-consummated wives.

Core Idea
Sunnah divorce requires one divorce and, for consummated wives, a pure period without intercourse.

Divorce in Islam is not a mere termination of marriage; it has a recommended method that aligns with the Prophet's practice. This passage from al-Quduri outlines two dimensions of the 'sunnah' in divorce: the number of divorces and the timing. Understanding these ensures that a divorce is effected in a way that is legally sound and minimizes harm, especially regarding the wife's waiting period ('idda).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two aspects
The passage opens by stating that the sunnah in divorce has two aspects: sunnah in number (al-idad) and sunnah in time (al-waqt). Recognize that these are separate rulings.
The term 'sunnah' here refers to the recommended method, not the act itself.
2
State the ruling for number
The sunnah in number is one divorce (talaq wahid), equally for a consummated wife (madkhul biha) and a non-consummated wife (ghayr madkhul biha). This is based on the practice of the early Muslims reported by Ibrahim al-Nakha'i.
3
State the ruling for time for consummated wives
For a wife with whom intercourse has occurred, the sunnah in time requires that the divorce be pronounced in a state of purity (tuhr) during which no intercourse has taken place. This ensures that the 'idda begins with a pure period.
The proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar, where the Prophet instructed him to take his wife back and wait for a pure period before divorcing.
4
State the ruling for time for non-consummated wives
For a wife who has not been consummated, there is no 'idda period, so she may be divorced even during menstruation. The passage supports this with the statement of al-Thawri.
This is because the purpose of the timing is to facilitate the counting of the 'idda, which is irrelevant here.
5
Understand the evidence
Both aspects are supported by proofs: the sunnah in number by the practice of the early Muslims (athar), and the sunnah in time by the hadith of Ibn Umar (Sunnah). Recognize that the Hanafi school relies on these to establish the recommended method.
The hadith is ahad (single narration) but its meaning is clear (dalala qati).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الطَّلَاقِ

ه وَالسُّنَّةُ فِي الطَّلَاقِ مِنْ وَجْهَيْنِ سُنَّةٌ فِي الْوَقْتِ وَسُنَّةٌ فِي الْعَدَدِ لا فَالسُّنَّةُ فِي الْعَدَدِ يَسْتَوِي فِيهَا الْمَدْخُولُ بِمَا وَغَيْرُ الْمَدْخُولِ بِمَا كوَالسُّنَّةُ فِي الْوَقْتِ تَثْبُتُ فِي الْمَدْخُولِ بِمَا خَاصَّةً وَهُوَ أَنْ يُطَلَّقَهَا فِي طُهْرٍ لَمْ يُجَامِعْهَا فِيهِ وَغَيْرُ الْمَدْخُولِ بِمَا يُطَلِّقُهَا فِي حَالَةِ الظُّهْرِ وَالْخَيْضِ

فِ

د وجه (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت فَالسُّنَّةُ فِي الْعَدَدِ يَسْتَوِي فِيهَا الْمَدْخُولُ بِمَا عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ قَالَ: «كَانُوا يَسْتَحِبُّونَ أَنْ يُطَلَّقَهَا وَاحِدَةً، ثُمَّ يَتْرُكَهَا حَتَّى تَحِيضَ ثَلَاثَ حِيَضِ» (مصنف ابن شيبه: ما يستحب من طلاق السنة، وكيف هو ؟ ، نمبر 17743 مصنف عبد الرزاق: باب وجه الطلاق وهو طلاق العدة والسنة، نمبر 10926)

وجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَالسُّنَّةُ فِي الْوَقْتِ تَثْبُتُ فِي الْمَدْخُولِ بِمَا خَاصَّةً أَعَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْن عُمَرَ رضي الله عنهما، «أَنَّهُ طَلَّقَ امْرَأَتَهُ وَهِيَ حَائِضٌ عَلَى عَهْدِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم ثُمَّ لِيُمْسِكُهَا حَقَّ تَطْهُرَ، ثُمَّ تَحِيضَ ثُمَّ تَطْهُرَ، ثُمَّ إِنْ شَاءَ أَمْسَكَ بَعْدُ، وَإِنْ شَاءَ طَلَّقَ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَمَ، فَتِلْكَ الْعِدَّةُ الَّتِي أَمَرَ اللهُ أَنْ تُطَلَّقَ لَهَا النِّسَاءُ.» (بخاري شريف: باب قول الله تعالى يا أيها النبي إذا
طلقتم النساء فطلقوهن لعدتهن، نمبر 5251 ابوداؤد شريف: باب في طلاق السنة، 2179)

د وجه (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَغَيْرُ الْمَدْخُولِ بِمَا يُطَلِقُهَا فِي حَالَةِ الظُّهْرِ وَالخَيْضِ \ عَن الثَّوْرِيِّ فِي رَجُلٍ طَلَّقَ الْبِكْرَ حَائِضًا قَالَ: «لَا بَأْسَ بِهِ لِأَنَّهُ لَا عِدَّةَ لَهَا»(مصنف عبدالرزاق: باب هل يطلق الرجل البكر حائضا؟ نمبر 10975)
Book of Divorce. And the sunnah in divorce is in two aspects: a sunnah in time and a sunnah in number. As for the sunnah in number, it is equal for the one who has had intercourse and the one who has not. And the sunnah in time is confirmed specifically for the one who has had intercourse, and it is that he divorces her in a state of purity in which he has not had intercourse with her. As for the one who has not had intercourse, he divorces her in the state of pregnancy or menstruation. [Then follows proof from Ibrahim: they used to recommend one divorce then leave her until three menstrual periods. Proof from Ibn Umar hadith: he divorced his wife while menstruating, then the Prophet ordered him to take her back, etc. Proof from al-Thawri: no harm in divorcing a virgin while menstruating because she has no waiting period.]
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage is a statement of the sunnah method of divorce according to the Hanafi school. It opens by stating that the sunnah in divorce has two aspects: number and time. The sunnah in number is one divorce (talaq wahid) for both a wife who has been consummated (madkhul biha) and one who has not (ghayr madkhul biha). This is proven by the practice of the early Muslims reported by Ibrahim al-Nakha'i. The sunnah in time applies specifically to a wife who has been consummated: the husband must divorce her in a period of purity (tuhr) during which he has not had intercourse with her. This is based on the well-known hadith of Ibn Umar, where the Prophet commanded him to take his wife back after divorcing her during her menses, then wait until she becomes pure, then menstruates again, then becomes pure, then if he wishes he may divorce her before touching her. This ensures the wife begins her waiting period (idda) in a state of purity. For a non-consummated wife, there is no waiting period, so she may be divorced even during menstruation, as stated by al-Thawri. The Hanafi school follows these rulings, making the one divorce in a pure period the recommended method.

Key Terms
السُّنَّةُ فِي الطَّلَاقِ (al-sunnatu fi al-talaq): The recommended method of divorce according to the Prophet's practice, which includes both the timing and the number of divorces.
الْمَدْخُولُ بِمَا (al-madkhulu biha): The wife with whom the husband has had sexual intercourse (consummated the marriage).
طُهْر (tuhr): A period of purity from menstruation; the time between two menstrual cycles when the woman is not menstruating.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Three divorces in one sitting
B) One divorce
C) Two divorces separated by a month
D) One divorce for consummated wife, two for virgin

Key Takeaway
The sunnah divorce is defined by its number (one) and its timing (pure period without intercourse for consummated wives).

Divorce of a Woman Who Does Not Menstruate
Ruling on divorcing a non-menstruating woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on divorcing a non-menstruating woman and identify the Quranic and hadith proofs that establish the ruling.

Core Idea
A non-menstruating woman may be divorced at any time, even after intercourse, because her 'idda is three months.

This lesson addresses a specific situation: when a woman does not menstruate due to youth or old age. The Hanafi school provides a clear sunnah method for divorcing such a woman, supported by a direct Quranic verse and a statement from the early scholar al-Zuhri. We will explore the ruling, its proofs, and the practical implication that no waiting period is needed between intercourse and divorce.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State the Hanafi position: the sunnah is one divorce at any time for a non-menstruating woman. Note that it is permissible (mubah) to divorce at any time without separation.
The act of divorcing itself is mubah; the sunnah method makes it recommended.
2
Examine the Quranic Proof
Read the verse from Surah At-Talaq (65:4). Identify that the 'idda for non-menstruating women is three months. This implies divorce can occur at any time since the 'idda does not depend on menstrual purity.
The verse is qat'i al-thubut and qat'i al-dalala in establishing the 'idda, but the inference about timing is based on the absence of a condition.
3
Consider the Hadith Proof
Review the statement from al-Zuhri: 'her divorce is one each month.' This reinforces that the month is the unit of 'idda, not menstrual periods.
This is a mursal hadith but accepted in Hanafi fiqh for such matters.
4
Understand the Practical Implication
Apply the ruling: a husband may divorce his non-menstruating wife immediately after intercourse without waiting. Her 'idda will be three lunar months from the date of divorce.
This differs from the menstruating woman who must be divorced in a pure period.
5
Note the Absence of Dispute
This ruling is agreed upon (muttafaq alayh) among the Hanafi school and is the mufta bihi position. No significant intra-madhhab difference exists.
The ruling is straightforward for the two categories: pre-menarche and post-menopause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا كَانَتْ الْمَرْأَةُ لَا تَحِيضُ مِنْ صِغَرٍ أَوْ كِبَرِ وَأَرَادَ أَنْ يُطَلَّقَهَا لِلسُّنَّةِ طَلَّقَهَا وَاحِدَةً مَقَ شَاءَ

و وجه (1) الآية لثبوت وَإِذَا كَانَتْ الْمَرْأَةُ لَا تَحِيضُ مِنْ صِغَرًا وَالَّتِي يَسْنَ مِنَ الْمَحِيضِ مِن نِّسَآبِكُمْ إِنِ ارْتَبْتُمْ فَعِدَّتُهُنَّ ثَلَثَةُ أَشْهُرٍ (سورة الطلاق 65، الآية، نمبر 3)

وجه: (٢)قول التابعي لثبوت وَإِذَا كَانَتْ الْمَرْأَةُ لَا تَحِيضُ مِنْ صِغَرِاعَنِ الزُّهْرِيِّ: فِي الْبِكْرِ الَّتِي لَم تَحضَ، وَالَّتِي قَعَدَتْ مِنَ الحَيْض: «طَلَاقُهَا كُلَّ هِلَالٍ تَطْلِيقَةٌ» (مصنف عبدالرزاق: باب طلاق التي لم تحض،نمبر 11112)

اصول: جس عورت کو حیض نہ آتا ہو اس ہر ایک ماہ ایک حیض کے درجہ میں شمار ہو گا۔

وَيَجُوزُ أَنْ يُطَلَّقَهَا وَلَا يَفْصِلُ بَيْنَ وَطْئِهَا وَطَلَاقِهَا بِزَمَانٍ
And if the woman does not menstruate due to young age or old age, and he intends to divorce her according to the sunnah, he divorces her with one divorce whenever he wishes. And proof: the verse 'and those who have despaired of menstruation among your women, if you doubt, their waiting period is three months' (Surah At-Talaq 65:4). And proof from al-Zuhri: for a virgin who has not menstruated and one who has ceased menstruation: 'her divorce is one each month.' Principle: For a woman who does not menstruate, each month is counted as one menstrual period. And it is permissible to divorce her without separating between intercourse and divorce by time.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling for a woman who does not menstruate, either because she is too young (pre-pubescent) or too old (post-menopausal). The sunnah in her case is one divorce at any time, without restriction to a specific period. The primary proof is the Quranic verse from Surah At-Talaq (65:4) which prescribes three months as the waiting period for such women, implying that divorce can happen at any time in terms of purity. The hadith of al-Zuhri states that her divorce is one per month (with each month considered a menstrual period). The Urdu principle clarifies that each lunar month is equivalent to one menstrual cycle for counting 'idda. Furthermore, it is permissible to divorce such a woman immediately after intercourse without waiting, since her 'idda is by months, not by menstrual periods, and there is no risk of confusion from a possible pregnancy. This ruling highlights the flexibility granted to women who do not menstruate.

Key Terms
لا تَحِيضُ (la tahidu): She does not menstruate, either due to young age (pre-menarche) or old age (post-menopause).
عِدَّةُ أَشْهُرٍ (iddatu ashur): A waiting period measured in months, applicable to women who do not menstruate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A non-menstruating woman may be divorced at any time without waiting for a purity period, and her 'idda is three lunar months.

Divorce of a Pregnant Woman: Number of Divorces
Ruling on divorcing a pregnant woman with an intra-Hanafi dispute on the number

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the number of divorces for a pregnant woman and explain the evidence for each view.

Core Idea
A pregnant woman may be divorced immediately, but the sunnah number divides the Hanafi school.

The Hanafi school universally permits divorcing a pregnant woman immediately after intercourse. However, a dispute arose among the early imams concerning the sunnah number of divorces to give her. This lesson examines the arguments of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf versus Muhammad al-Shaybani and Zufar, and clarifies the relied-upon position for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the agreed ruling
All Hanafi imams agree that divorcing a pregnant woman is valid immediately after intercourse, because the womb is closed, preventing a second pregnancy.
This removes the condition of waiting for purity (tuhr).
2
Identify the disputed issue
The dispute is about the sunnah number: three divorces with monthly intervals (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) versus a single divorce until delivery (Muhammad and Zufar).
The term 'sunnah' here means the recommended method, not a binding requirement.
3
Examine the majority proof (Abu Hanifa & Abu Yusuf)
They rely on the practice of al-Zuhri, who analogized the pregnant woman's 'idda to monthly periods, allowing three divorces spaced by a month.
The evidence is a report: 'I said to al-Zuhri... He said: According to the number of her menstrual periods.'
4
Examine the minority proof (Muhammad & Zufar)
They cite al-Hasan al-Basri: 'The pregnant woman is not given more than one divorce until she delivers.' Delivery ends the 'idda immediately, so only one divorce is needed.
This view prioritizes the direct link between 'idda and birth.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The school's later authorities (e.g., al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah) adopt the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: three divorces with monthly intervals are the sunnah.
Practically, a husband may give three divorces over two months, but if he gives only one, it is valid though not the optimal sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الـ وَطَلَاقُ الْحَامِلِ يَجُوزُ عَقِيبَ الجمَاعِ وَيُطَلِقُهَا لِلسُّنَّةِ ثَلَاثًا يَفْصِلُ بَيْنَ كُلِّ تَطْلِيقَتَيْنِ بِشَهْرٍ عِنْدَهُمَا. وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ وَزُفَرُ لَا يُطَلِّقُهَا لِلسُّنَّةِ إِلَّا وَاحِدَةً

وجه : (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَطَلَاقُ الْحَامِلِ يَجُوزُ عَقِيبَ الْحِمَاعِ اعَنِ الْحَسَنِ، وَمُحَمَّدٍ، قَالَا: «إِذَا كَانَتْ حَامِلًا طَلَّقَهَامَتَى شَاءَ» (مصنف ابن شيبه ماقالوافي الحامل كيف تطلق؟،نمبر 17748)

وجه (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَيُطَلَّقْهَا لِلسُّنَّةِ ثَلَاثًا \ قُلْتُ لِلزُّهْرِيِّ : إِذَا أَرَادَ أَنْ يُطَلَّقَهَا حَامِلًا ثَلَاثًا، كَيْفَ؟ قَالَ: «عَلَى عِدَّةِ أَقْرَائِهَا» (مصنف عبدالرزاق باب طلاق الحامل، نمبر 10932 مصنف عبدالرزاق: ما قالوا في الحامل كيف تطلق؟، نمبر 17750)

وجه : (٢) قول التابعى لثبوت وَيُطَلِقُهَا لِلسُّنَّةِ ثَلَاثًا اعَنِ الْحَسَنِ قَالَ: «لَا تُزَادُ الْحَامِلُ عَلَى تَطْلِيقَةٍ حَتَّى تَضَعَ، فَإِذَا وَضَعَتْ فَقَدْ بَانَتْ مِنْهُ» (مصنف عبدالرزاق باب طلاق الحامل، نمبر 10934 ، مصنف ابن شيبه ما قالوا في الحامل كيف تطلق؟نمبر 17746)
[And] divorce of the pregnant woman is permissible immediately after intercourse, and he divorces her according to the sunnah three times, separating between each two divorces by a month according to them. And Muhammad and Zufar said: He does not divorce her according to the sunnah except one. Proof: the statement of the follower regarding the permissibility of divorcing a pregnant woman immediately after intercourse: from al-Hasan and Muhammad, they said: 'If she is pregnant, he divorces her whenever he wishes.' Proof: the statement of the follower regarding divorcing her according to the sunnah three times: I said to al-Zuhri: If he intends to divorce her while pregnant three times, how? He said: 'According to the number of her menstrual periods.' Proof: the statement of the follower regarding divorcing her according to the sunnah three times: from al-Hasan, he said: 'The pregnant woman is not given more than one divorce until she delivers, and when she delivers, she has become completely separated from him.'
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the sunnah method of divorcing a pregnant woman. The text first states that divorce of a pregnant woman is permissible immediately after intercourse, and the majority view (ascribed to 'them', i.e., Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that the sunnah is to give three divorces, separating each by a month. This is supported by the practice reported from al-Zuhri, who likened her 'idda to menstrual cycles (months). However, Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani and Imam Zufar hold that the sunnah is only one divorce, based on a report from al-Hasan al-Basri that a pregnant woman should not receive more than one divorce until she delivers, because delivery concludes her 'idda immediately. The first position (three with monthly intervals) is the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school. The Urdu principle at the end of the page explains the permissibility of immediate divorce after intercourse because the womb is closed, preventing another pregnancy.

Key Terms
الْحَامِلِ (al-hamil): The pregnant woman; a wife who is carrying a child in her womb.
عَقِيبَ الجمَاعِ (aqiba al-jima'): Immediately after sexual intercourse, without any time delay.
شَهْر (shahr): A lunar month, used as a measure for the interval between divorces for a pregnant woman.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi), how should a husband divorce his pregnant wife following the sunnah?
A) One divorce immediately
B) Three divorces at once
C) Three divorces separated by a month each
D) Two divorces separated by two months

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi view permits immediate divorce of a pregnant woman and recommends three divorces spaced by a month; the minority holds only one until delivery.

Divorce of a Pregnant Woman: Immediate Permissibility and Sunnah Triple Divorce
Ruling on immediate divorce of pregnant woman and sunnah triple divorce with ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on immediate divorce of a pregnant woman and explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding the number of sunnah divorces.

Core Idea
A pregnant woman can be divorced immediately after intercourse; three separate divorces per month is sunnah according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

This passage from Kitab al-Talaq addresses two specific questions: can a husband divorce his pregnant wife immediately after intercourse, and what is the sunnah method for issuing three divorces to a pregnant woman? Understanding this ruling requires appreciating the role of iddah and the preservation of lineage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The passage states that immediate divorce of a pregnant woman is permissible (yajuz) and then discusses the sunnah method for triple divorce with monthly intervals.
The first ruling is unconditional permissibility; the second is a recommended method with an ikhtilaf.
2
Examine the evidence for immediate divorce
The author cites a statement from al-Hasan and Muhammad: 'If she is pregnant, divorce her whenever he wishes' (mata sha'a), indicating no temporal restriction.
The rationale: pregnancy eliminates the risk of confusion of lineage.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on triple divorce
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that three divorces can be given with monthly intervals; Muhammad and Zufar restrict to one divorce until delivery.
The difference hinges on whether the iddah of a pregnant woman (delivery) permits multiple intervals.
4
Evaluate the tarjih (preferred view)
The matn presents the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf first, indicating its weight; this is the mufta bihi position.
Later Hanafi works (e.g., Hidayah) adopt this view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الطَّلَاقِ
وَيَجُوزُ أَنْ يُطَلَّقَهَا وَلَا يَفْصِلُ بَيْنَ وَطْئِهَا وَطَلَاقِهَا بِزَمَانٍ وَطَلَاقُ الْحَامِلِ يَجُوزُ عَقِيبَ الْجِمَاعِ وَيُطَلِّقُهَا لِلسُّنَّةِ ثَلَاثًا يَفْصِلُ بَيْنَ كُلِّ تَطْلِيقَتَيْنِ بِشَهْرٍ عِنْدَهُمَا. وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ وَزُفَرُ لَا يُطَلِّقُهَا لِلسُّنَّةِ إِلَّا وَاحِدَةً
وجه : (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَطَلَاقُ الْحَامِلِ يَجُوزُ عَقِيبَ الْحِمَاعِ اعَنِ الْحَسَنِ، وَمُحَمَّدٍ، قَالَا: «إِذَا كَانَتْ حَامِلًا طَلَّقَهَامَتَى شَاءَ» (مصنف ابن شيبه ماقالوافي الحامل كيف تطلق؟،نمبر 17748)
وجه (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَيُطَلَّقْهَا لِلسُّنَّةِ ثَلَاثًا قُلْتُ لِلزُّهْرِيِّ : إِذَا أَرَادَ أَنْ يُطَلَّقَهَا حَامِلًا ثَلَاثًا، كَيْفَ؟ قَالَ: «عَلَى عِدَّةِ أَقْرَائِهَا» (مصنف عبدالرزاق باب طلاق الحامل، نمبر 10932 مصنف عبدالرزاق: ما قالوا في الحامل كيف تطلق؟، نمبر 17750)
وجه : (٢) قول التابعى لثبوت وَيُطَلِقُهَا لِلسُّنَّةِ ثَلَاثًا اعَنِ الْحَسَنِ قَالَ: «لَا تُزَادُ الْحَامِلُ عَلَى تَطْلِيقَةٍ حَتَّى تَضَعَ، فَإِذَا وَضَعَتْ فَقَدْ بَانَتْ مِنْهُ» (مصنف عبدالرزاق باب طلاق الحامل، نمبر 10934 ، مصنف ابن شيبه ما قالوا في الحامل كيف تطلق؟نمبر 17746)
اصول: حاملہ عورت کو جماع کے فورا بعد طلاق دیا جا سکتا ہے، کیونکہ رحم کا منہ بند ہے دوسرا حمل ممکن نہیں۔
Book of Divorce. It is permissible to divorce her without separating between intercourse and divorce by time, and divorce of a pregnant woman is permissible immediately after intercourse, and he divorces her according to sunnah three times, separating between every two divorces by a month according to them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). And Muhammad and Zufar said: He does not divorce her according to sunnah except once. (Proof 1: Statement of the tabi'i for establishing that divorce of a pregnant woman is permissible immediately after intercourse, from al-Hasan and Muhammad, they said: 'If she is pregnant, he divorces her whenever he wishes.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba) Proof 1: Statement of the tabi'i for establishing that he divorces her according to sunnah three times: I said to al-Zuhri: If he wants to divorce her while pregnant three times, how? He said: 'According to the number of her menstrual periods.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq) Proof 2: Statement of the tabi'i for establishing that he divorces her according to sunnah three times: from al-Hasan, he said: 'The pregnant woman is not given more than one divorce until she gives birth, and when she gives birth, she has become separated from him.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba) Principle: A pregnant woman can be divorced immediately after intercourse, because the mouth of the womb is closed, another pregnancy is not possible.)
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Talaq opens with two rulings. First, it clarifies that a man may divorce his pregnant wife immediately after intercourse without needing to wait any time. This is because pregnancy itself is a visible sign of the waiting period (iddah). Second, it discusses the sunnah method of divorce for a pregnant woman: according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, a husband can issue three separate divorces across three months, one per month. However, Muhammad al-Shaybani and Zufar hold that only one divorce is sunnah for a pregnant woman, as her iddah ends at delivery and three divorces would be excessive. The hadith proofs from tabi'un support both positions: some allow three divorces at monthly intervals, others restrict to one. The Urdu summary reiterates that immediate divorce of a pregnant woman is permissible because her womb is closed, making another pregnancy impossible, so there is no risk of confusion of lineage.

Key Terms
طلاق السنة (ṭalāq al-sunnah): A divorce that conforms to the sunnah, i.e., issued during a period of purity without intercourse, or for a pregnant woman at monthly intervals.
الحامل (al-ḥāmil): A pregnant woman whose pregnancy is established; her iddah ends at delivery.
عقب الجماع (ʿuqayb al-jimāʿ): Immediately after sexual intercourse, without any intervening period.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, how should a husband divorce his pregnant wife in accordance with sunnah?
A) He may issue three divorces in one sitting.
B) He should issue one divorce and wait for delivery.
C) He issues three divorces, each separated by a month.
D) He must wait until after delivery to divorce.

Key Takeaway
Immediate divorce of a pregnant woman is permissible, and the sunnah method for triple divorce is monthly intervals according to the predominant Hanafi view.

Divorce During Menstruation: Valid but Prohibited
Ruling on the validity of divorce during menses and recommended action

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on divorce during menstruation and apply the recommended action of taking her back.

Core Idea
Divorce during menses is valid but sinful; the husband must take her back and wait for two clean periods.

A husband may divorce his wife at any time, but not all times are equal. Divorcing a menstruating wife is prohibited, yet the divorce takes effect. This lesson examines the ruling, its basis in the hadith of Ibn Umar, and the proper procedure to correct the mistake.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The act is divorcing a wife while she is in menstruation. Determine the hukm (ruling) for the act itself and for the effectiveness of the divorce.
Hanafi: the divorce is sahih (valid) but the act is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked).
2
Locate the Dalil
The proof is the hadith of Abdullah ibn Umar. Find the key phrases in the hadith that indicate the divorce is valid and that the husband is ordered to take her back.
The Prophet (peace be upon him) did not nullify the divorce but ordered ruju' (taking back).
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
How does the hadith prove the divorce is valid? The Prophet's instruction to 'take her back' implies the divorce had already occurred. His command to wait for two clean periods shows the proper sunnah procedure.
If the divorce were void, he would have ordered a new marriage, not a revocation.
4
Note the Recommended Action
The husband is recommended (mustahabb) to revoke the divorce (yurājiʿuhā) during her iddah. Then he must wait for her to become pure, menstruate, and become pure again before divorcing properly if he wishes.
This is to align with the sunnah and avoid sin.
5
Differentiate Between Ruling and Sin
The divorce is legally effective despite being forbidden. The sin is on the husband for the timing, but the marital bond is severed unless he takes her back.
This distinction is crucial for understanding fiqh: an act can be valid yet sinful.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا طَلَّقَ امْرَأَتَهُ فِي حَالِ الْحَيْضِ وَقَعَ الطَّلَاقُ وَيُسْتَحَبُّ لَهُ أَنْ يُرَاجِعَهَا فَإِنْ طَهُرَتْ وَحَاضَتْ ثُمَّ طَهُرَتْ فَإِنْ شَاءَ طَلَّقَهَا وَإِنْ شَاءَ أَمْسَكَهَا
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا طَلَّقَ امْرَأَتَهُ فِي حَالِ الْخَيْضِ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عُمَرَ رضي عنهما، «أَنَّهُ طَلَّقَ امْرَأَتَهُ وَهِيَ حَائِضٌ عَلَى عَهْدِ رَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَسَأَلَ عُمَرُ بْنُ الْخَطَّابِ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَنْ ذَلِكَ، فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم : مُرْهُ فَلْيُرَاجِعْهَا، ثُمَّ لِيُمْسِكُهَا حَتَّى تَطْهُرَ، ثُمَّ تَحِيضَ، ثُمَّ تَطْهُرَ، ثُمَّ إِنْ شَاءَ أَمْسَكَ بَعْدُ، وَإِنْ شَاءَ طَلَّقَ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَمَسَّ، فَتِلْكَ الْعِدَّةُ الَّتِي أَمَرَ اللَّهُ أَنْ تُطَلَّقَ لَهَا النِّسَاءُ.» (بخاري شريف: باب قول الله تعالى يا أيها النبي إذا طلقتم النساء فطلقوهن لعدتهن، نمبر 5251- مسلم شریف: (۱) - باب تحريم طلاق الحائض بغير رضاها، وأنه لو خالف وقع الطلاق ويؤمر برجعتها، نمبر1471 ابوداؤد شريف باب في طلاق السنة، نمبر 2179)
وجه : (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا طَلَّقَ امْرَأَتَهُ فِي حَالِ الخَيْضِ سَمِعْتُ ابْنَ عُمَرَ قَالَ: «طَلَّقَ عُمَرَ امْرَأَتَهُ وَهِيَ حَائِضٌ فَذَكَرَ عُمَرُ لِلنَّبِيِّ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فَقَالَ : لِيُرَاجِعْهَا. قُلْتُ: تُحْتَسَبُ. قَالَ: فَمَهْ» (بخاري شريف : باب إذا طلقت الحائض تعتد بذلك الطلاق ، نمبر 5252 مسلم شریف: (۱) -
And if he divorces his wife in the state of menstruation, the divorce occurs, and it is recommended for him to take her back. Then if she becomes pure, and menstruates, then becomes pure, then if he wishes he divorces her, and if he wishes he keeps her. (Proof 1: Hadith for establishing that if he divorces his wife during menses: from Abdullah ibn Umar, may Allah be pleased with them, that he divorced his wife while she was menstruating during the time of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), so Umar ibn al-Khattab asked the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) about that, so he said: 'Order him to take her back, then keep her until she becomes pure, then menstruates, then becomes pure, then if he wishes he may keep her after that, and if he wishes he may divorce before touching. That is the iddah which Allah commanded that women be divorced for it.' (Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud)) (Proof 2: Hadith for establishing that if he divorces his wife during menses: I heard Ibn Umar say: 'Umar divorced his wife while she was menstruating, so Umar mentioned that to the Prophet (peace be upon him), and he said: 'Let him take her back.' I said: 'Shall it be counted?' He said: 'What else?' (Bukhari, Muslim))
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage presents a key ruling: if a husband divorces his wife while she is menstruating, the divorce is legally valid (it falls) even though it is prohibited. The husband is strongly recommended (mustahabb) to revoke the divorce and take her back. The correct sunnah procedure is to wait until she becomes pure (after menses), then if she menstruates again and becomes pure again, he may either keep her or divorce her before intercourse. This is the proper iddah-period divorce. The supporting hadith from Ibn Umar and the Prophet's instruction provide the basis. Note that the divorce counts even though it was done at a forbidden time; the sin is on the husband for divorcing during menses, but the divorce itself is not null.

Key Terms
الحائض (al-ḥāʾiḍ): A woman in the state of menstruation.
يراجعها (yurājiʿuhā): To take her back (revoke the divorce) during the iddah period.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a husband divorces his wife while she is menstruating?
A) The divorce does not take effect and is void.
B) The divorce takes effect but the husband must take her back and wait for proper period.
C) The divorce takes effect and the husband cannot revoke it.
D) The husband must repeat the divorce after her menses.

Key Takeaway
A divorce during menstruation is legally valid but sinful; the husband must revoke it and follow the sunnah procedure.

Conditions for Valid Divorce: Adulthood, Sanity, and Slave's Authority
Conditions for valid divorce (capacity and authority)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid divorce regarding capacity (adulthood and sanity) and the slave's own authority, and apply the proofs (hadith, companion statements, Quran) to justify these rulings.

Core Idea
Divorce is valid only from an adult, sane husband; a minor or insane person's divorce is void; a slave's divorce is his own, not his master's.

The validity of divorce hinges on the legal capacity of the husband. This passage from al-Quduri clarifies three key conditions: the husband must be adult and sane, and if he is a slave, he retains independent authority over his divorce. We will examine the proofs from hadith, companion statements, and Quran that establish these foundational Hanafi principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three subjects and their rulings
Read the passage and note the rulings: the divorce of a minor and an insane person does not take effect; the divorce of a slave does take effect, while his master's divorce of the slave's wife does not.
2
Analyze the proof for the minor and insane
Locate the hadith 'the pen is lifted from three' (Ali, marfu'). Understand that 'rafi'a al-qalam' means their actions have no legal effect. Also note supporting companion statements and Quran 2:286.
The hadith is sahih and widely transmitted.
3
Analyze the proof for the slave's divorce
Find the hadith of Ibn Abbas and the statement of Ibn Umar. The Prophet said divorce belongs to 'the one who takes hold of the leg' — meaning the one directly involved in the marriage. The master's authority does not extend to dissolving the slave's marriage.
4
Extract the usul principles
The passage ends with two principles: (1) Without intellect and puberty, contracts and dissolutions are invalid. (2) Divorce is considered only from the one who holds the marital tie.
These principles are derived from the proofs and apply broadly in Hanafi fiqh.
5
Apply to a hypothetical scenario
Consider: a minor boy married with guardian's permission tries to divorce his wife. The divorce is void because he lacks capacity. Similarly, a master cannot divorce his slave's wife even if he dislikes her.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَقَعُ طَلَاقُ كُلِّ زَوْجٍ إِذَا كَانَ بَالِغًا عَاقِلًا وَلَا يَقَعُ طَلَاقُ الصَّبِيِّ وَالْمَجْنُونِ وَإِذَا تَزَوَّجَ الْعَبْدُ ثُمَّ طَلَّقَ امْرَأَتَهُ وَقَعَ طَلَاقُهُ وَلَا يَقَعُ طَلَاقُ مَوْلَاهُ عَلَى امْرَأَتِهِ
وجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَقَعُ طَلَاقُ الصَّبِيِّ وَالْمَجْنُونِ عَنْ عَلِي عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «رُفِعَ الْقَلَمُ عَنْ ثَلَاثَةٍ عَنِ النَّائِمِ حَتَّى يَسْتَيْقِظَ وَعَنِ الصَّبِيِّ حَتَّى يَحْتَلِمَ، وَعَنِ الْمَجْنُونِ حَتَّى يَعْقِل» (ابوداؤد شریف : باب في المجنون يسرق أو يصيب حدا ، نمبر 4403 بخاري شريف: باب الطلاق في الإغلاق، نمبر 5269 نسائي شريف: 3432)
وجه (۲) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَلا يَقَعُ طَلَاقُ الصَّيَ وَالْمَجْنُونِ وَقَالَ عُثْمَانُ لَيْسَ لِمَجْنُونِ وَلَا لِسَكْرَانَ طَلَاقٌ وَقَالَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسِ طَلَاقُ السَّكْرَانِ وَالْمُسْتَكْرَهِ لَيْسَ بِجَائِرٍ وَقَالَ عُقْبَةُ بْنُ عَامِرٍ لَا يَجُوزُ طَلَاقُ الْمُوَسْوس (بخاري شريف : باب الطلاق في الإغلاق، نمبر 5269)
وجه (۳) الآية لثبوت وَلَا يَقَعُ طَلَاقُ الصَّيَ وَالْمَجْنُونِ رَبَّنَا لَا تُؤَاخِذْنَا إِن نَّسِينَا أَوْ أَخْطَأْنَا (القرآن، سورة البقرة2، الآية، نمبر 286)
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا تَزَوَّجَ الْعَبْدُ ثُمَّ طَلَّقَ امْرَأَتَهُ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، قَالَ: أَتَى النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم رَجُلٌ، فَقَالَ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، إِنَّ سَيِّدِي زَوَّجَنِي أَمَتَهُ، وَهُوَ يُرِيدُ أَنْ يُفَرِّقَ بَيْنِي وَبَيْنَهَا، قَالَ: فَصَعِدَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم الْمِنْبَرَ، فَقَالَ: «يَا أَيُّهَا النَّاسُ، مَا بَالُ أَحَدِكُمْ يُزَوِّجُ عَبْدَهُ أَمَتَهُ، ثُمَّ يُرِيدُ أَنْ يُفَرِّقَ بَيْنَهُمَا ، إِنَّمَا الطَّلَاقُ لِمَنْ أَخَذَ بِالسَّاقِ» (ابن ماجه شریف: (۳۱) باب طلاق العبد،نمبر 2081 دارقطني: : ١٦ - كتاب الطلاق والخلع والإيلاء وغيره،نمبر 3901)
وجه (۲) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَإِذَا تَزَوَّجَ الْعَبْدُ ثُمَّ طَلَّقَ امْرَأَتَهُ أَنَّ ابْنَ عُمَرَ رضي الله عنهما كَانَ يَقُولُ: " مَنْ أَذِنَ لِعَبْدِهِ أَنْ يَنْكِحَ فَالطَّلَاقُ بِيَدِ الْعَبْدِ، لَيْسَ بِيَدِ غَيْرِهِ مِنْ طَلَاقِهِ شَيْءٌ " (سنن بيهقي : باب طلاق العبد بغير إذن سيده،نمبر 15114)
اصول: بغیر عقل اور بلوغ کے عقود و فسوخ واقع نہیں ہوتی اور نہ شریعت اسکا اعتبار کرتی ہے۔ اصول: جس کی بیوی ہو اسی کی طلاق معتبر ہو گی۔ مولی کی طلاق غلام کی بیوی پر نہیں واقع ہو گی۔
And the divorce of every husband takes effect if he is an adult, sane; and the divorce of a minor and an insane person does not take effect. And if a slave marries, then divorces his wife, his divorce takes effect, and the divorce of his master upon his wife does not take effect. (Proof 1: Hadith establishing that the divorce of a minor and insane does not take effect: from Ali from the Prophet (peace be upon him), he said: 'The pen is lifted from three: from the sleeping person until he wakes, from the minor until he dreams (becomes mature), and from the insane until he becomes sane.' (Abu Dawud, Bukhari, Nasa'i)) (Proof 2: Statement of the companion establishing that the divorce of a minor and insane does not take effect: Uthman said: 'There is no divorce for an insane person nor for an intoxicated person.' Ibn Abbas said: 'The divorce of an intoxicated person and one forced is not valid.' Uqba ibn Amir said: 'The divorce of a obsessed person is not valid.' (Bukhari)) (Proof 3: Verse establishing that the divorce of a minor and insane does not take effect: 'Our Lord, do not hold us accountable if we forget or err.' (Quran 2:286)) (Proof 1: Hadith establishing that if a slave marries then divorces his wife: from Ibn Abbas, he said: A man came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and said: 'O Messenger of Allah, my master married me to his female slave, and he wants to separate between me and her.' He said: So the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) ascended the pulpit and said: 'O people, what is the matter with one of you who marries his slave to his female slave, then wants to separate between them? Indeed, divorce is only for the one who takes hold of the leg.' (Ibn Majah, Darqutni)) (Proof 2: Statement of the companion establishing that if a slave marries then divorces his wife: Ibn Umar, may Allah be pleased with them, used to say: 'Whoever permits his slave to marry, then divorce is in the hand of the slave; nothing of his divorce is in the hand of anyone else.' (Bayhaqi)) Principles: Without intellect and puberty, contracts and cancellations do not take effect, and the Shariah does not consider them. Principle: Divorce is considered only from the one who has the wife; the master's divorce does not fall upon the slave's wife.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage establishes three foundational principles for the validity of divorce: capacity, and the slave's independent authority. First, divorce is only effective from a husband who is adult (baligh) and sane (aqil). The Prophet's hadith 'the pen is lifted from three' confirms that minors and the insane are not legally responsible, so their divorces are void. Companions like Uthman and Ibn Abbas also affirm this, and the Quranic verse about forgetfulness and error reinforces that actions lacking full intent are not held against one. Second, if a slave marries with his master's permission, he has the authority to divorce his wife; the master cannot divorce the slave's wife. The hadith of the Prophet 'Innama al-talaq li man akhadha bi al-saq' (divorce belongs to the one who takes the leg) is interpreted to mean that only the one who is directly involved in the marital relationship can divorce. Ibn Umar's statement further clarifies. The Urdu summary reiterates: without reason and majority, contracts and dissolutions are invalid; and the master's divorce does not affect the slave's wife.

Key Terms
الصبي (al-ṣabiyy): A minor who has not reached puberty (ihtilam).
المجنون (al-majnūn): An insane person who lacks reason ('aql).
العبد (al-ʿabd): A slave who may own property and marry with master's permission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a minor boy utters a divorce, what is the ruling according to Hanafi fiqh?
A) The divorce is valid if he understands the meaning.
B) The divorce is not valid because he lacks legal capacity.
C) The divorce is valid only with guardian's consent.
D) The divorce is valid but must be confirmed by a judge.

Key Takeaway
Divorce is only valid from a husband who is adult, sane, and — if a slave — acting on his own authority; a minor, insane person, or master of a slave cannot effect divorce.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
