Kitab al-Raj'ah: Condition of Halalah is Makruh
Note on halalah ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on halalah and distinguish between conditional and unconditional marriage.

Core Idea
Marriage with the condition of halalah is makruh and sinful; without condition, it is valid but the woman becomes lawful only after consummation.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on halalah—the process of a triply divorced woman becoming lawful for her first husband by marrying and divorcing a second husband. The text distinguishes two scenarios: one with the explicit condition of halalah and one without. Understanding this distinction is essential to avoid a sinful arrangement while recognizing the validity of a genuine second marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
Halalah: a woman divorced by triple talaq marries a second man to become lawful for her first husband.
2
Note the condition
Distinguish between marriage with an explicit condition of halalah and marriage without such condition.
The condition can be verbal or written.
3
State the ruling for each case
With condition: makruh and sinful. Without condition: valid and permissible.
Sin (ithm) is incurred only when the condition is explicit.
4
Identify the additional requirements
The second marriage must be consummated, then divorced, and the woman completes iddah before remarrying the first husband.
This is the 'new permission' referred to in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الرَّجْعَةِ
اصول: حلالہ کی شرط پر نکاح مکروہ اور گناہ ہے، البتہ بغیر شرط کے نکاح کے بعد مطلقہ ہو کر زوج اول کے لئے حلال ہو سکتی ہے۔ اصول عورت زوج ثانی وطی کراکر حل جدید کیساتھ آئے گی ۔
Book of Revocable Divorce. Principle: Marriage on condition of halalah is disliked and sinful. However, without condition, after marriage and being divorced, she can become lawful for the first husband. Principle: The woman, after intercourse with the second husband, will come with a new permission.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This is a brief note on the ruling of halalah (making a woman lawful for her first husband after a triple divorce). The text states that it is makruh (disliked) and sinful to contract a marriage with the explicit condition that the purpose is to make the wife lawful for her first husband. However, if a woman marries a second husband without any such condition, the marriage is valid, and if she is later divorced by him (after consummation) and completes her iddah, she becomes lawful for her first husband. The principle is that the woman must have actual intercourse with the second husband, and then she comes with a new permission (i.e., a fresh marriage contract with the first husband is required). This reflects the Hanafi position that halalah is not a praiseworthy act and is discouraged when pre-arranged.

Key Terms
حلالہ (halalah): The act of making a divorced woman lawful for her first husband through marriage to a second husband and subsequent divorce.
مطلقہ (mutallaqah): A woman who has been divorced
زوج اول (zawj awwal): First husband

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is permissible and recommended
B) It is makruh and sinful
C) It is haram and invalid
D) It is mubah with no sin

Key Takeaway
Marriage on condition of halalah is makruh and sinful; without condition, it is valid only after consummation.

Book of Ila': Definition, Ruling, and Proofs
Ruling with proof: definition and consequence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of ila', explain its Hanafi ruling, and identify the Quran, hadith, and Companion proofs that establish it.

Core Idea
Ila' is a binding oath of abstinence; if unfulfilled after four months, it triggers a ba'in divorce.

This lesson introduces Kitab al-Ila' from Al-Quduri's matn. Ila' is when a husband swears an oath to abstain from sexual relations with his wife for at least four months. The Hanafi school holds that if he returns within that period, he must pay kaffarah for breaking his oath; if he does not, a single ba'in divorce automatically takes effect after the four months. The text provides three categories of proof: the Quranic verse (2:226-227), a hadith of the Prophet's own ila', and the saying of Ibn Abbas. Understanding these proofs will ground your knowledge of this important family law ruling.

Guided Path
1
Define Ila' and the Muli
Identify the husband's statement that constitutes ila'—an oath to avoid intercourse for four months or more. Recognize that the husband becomes a muli upon making such an oath.
The oath can be any wording that implies abstinence; it does not require a specific formula.
2
Identify the Two Possible Outcomes
Track the two scenarios: (1) if the husband has intercourse within four months, he breaks his oath, owes kaffarah, and the ila' is cancelled; (2) if he does not, after four months a ba'in divorce occurs.
Kaffarah is the standard expiation for breaking an oath (feeding/clothing ten poor or fasting three days).
3
Analyze the Proofs (Quran, Hadith, Companion Saying)
Examine the primary verse (2:226-227) which establishes the four-month waiting period and the alternatives of return or divorce. Then consider the hadith (Bukhari) where the Prophet made ila', confirming its validity. Finally, note Ibn Abbas's statement that ila' is only valid with an oath.
Each proof serves a different function: the verse provides the framework, the hadith shows prophetic practice, and the Companion saying clarifies a condition.
4
Understand the Hanafi Ruling on Automatic Divorce
Recognize that the Hanafi school holds that if four months pass without return, the divorce (ba'in) occurs automatically without court intervention. This is derived from the verse's phrase 'if they resolve on divorce' implying that the passage of time constitutes resolve.
Other schools require a court order; this is a key madhhab difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْإِيلَاءِ
قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ - إِذَا قَالَ الزَّوْجُ لِامْرَأَتِهِ وَاللَّهِ لَا أَقْرَبُكِ أَوْ وَاللَّهِ لَا أَقْرَبُكِ أَرْبَعَةَ أَشْهُرٍ فَهُوَ مُولٍ فَإِنْ وَطِئَهَا فِي الْأَرْبَعَةِ الْأَشْهُرِ حَنِثَ فِي يَمِينِهِ وَلَزِمَتْهُ الْكَفَّارَةُ وَسَقَطَ الْإِيلَاءُ
وجه: (1) الآية لثبوت إِذَا قَالَ الزَّوْجُ لِامْرَأَتِهِ وَاللَّهِ لَا أَقْرَبُكِ لِلَّذِينَ يُؤْلُونَ مِن نِّسَآئِهِمْ تَرَبُّصُ أَرْبَعَةِ أَشْهُرٍ فَإِن فَآءُوا فَإِنَّ اللَّهَ غَفُورٌ رَّحِيمٌ * وَإِنْ عَزَمُوا الطَّلَاقَ فَإِنَّ اللَّهَ سَمِيعٌ عَلِيمٌ (القرآن سورة البقرة 2، الآية 226/227)
وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت إِذَا قَالَ الزَّوْجُ لِامْرَأَتِهِ وَاللَّهِ لَا أَقْرَبُكِ سَمِعَ أَنَسَ بْنَ مَالِكٍ يَقُولُ: «آلَى رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم مِنْ نِسَائِهِ وَكَانَتِ انْفَكَّتْ رِجْلُهُ فَأَقَامَ فِي مَشْرُبَةٍ لَهُ تِسْعًا وَعِشْرِينَ، ثُمَّ نَزَلَ، فَقَالُوا: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ آلَيْتَ شَهْرًا، فَقَالَ: الشَّهْرُ تِسْعٌ وَعِشْرُونَ.» (بخاري شريف: باب قول الله تعالى للذين يؤلون من نسائهم تربص أربعة أشهر، نمبر 5289)
وجه (۳) قول الصحابي لثبوت إِذَا قَالَ الزَّوْجُ لِامْرَأَتِهِ وَاللَّهِ لَا أَقْرَبُكِ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: «لَا إِيلَاءَ إِلَّا بِحَلِفٍ» (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة: من قال لا إيلاء إلا بحلف، نمبر 18630)
لوجه: (1) الآية لثبوت فَإِنْ وَطِئَهَا فِي الْأَرْبَعَةِ الْأَشْهُرِ ذَلِكَ كَفَّارَةُ أَيْمَانِكُمْ إِذَا حَلَفْتُمْ وَاحْفَظُوا أَيْمَانَكُمْ كَذَلِكَ يُبَيِّنُ اللَّهُ لَكُمْ آيَاتِهِ لَعَلَّكُمْ تَشْكُرُونَ (القرآن سورة المائدة 5، الآية 89)
وجه (٢) الآية لثبوت فَإِنْ وَطِئَهَا فِي الْأَرْبَعَةِ الْأَشْهُرِ وَلِلَّذِينَ يُؤْلُونَ مِن نِّسَآئِهِمْ تَرَبُّصُ أَرْبَعَةِ أَشْهُرٍ فَإِن فَآءُوا فَإِنَّ اللَّهَ غَفُورٌ رَّحِيمٌ (القرآن سورة البقرة 2، الآية 226)
وجه (۳) قول الصحابي لثبوت فَإِنْ وَطِئَهَا فِي الْأَرْبَعَةِ الْأَشْهُرِ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ رضي الله عنهما فِي آيَةِ الْإِيلَاءِ قَالَ: «الرَّجُلُ يَحْلِفُ لِامْرَأَتِهِ بِاللَّهِ لَا يَنْكِحُهَا تَتَرَبَّصُ أَرْبَعَةَ أَشْهُرٍ فَإِنْ هُوَ نَكَحَهَا كَفَّرَ عَنْ يَمِينِهِ بِإِطْعَامِ عَشَرَةِ مَسَاكِينَ أَوْ كِسْوَتِهِمْ أَوْ تَحْرِيرِ رَقَبَةٍ فَمَنْ لَمْ يَجِدْ فَصِيَامُ ثَلَاثَةِ أَيَّامٍ وَإِنْ مَضَتْ أَرْبَعَةُ أَشْهُرٍ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَنْكِحَهَا خَيَّرَهُ السُّلْطَانُ إِمَّا أَنْ يُفِيءَ فَيُرَاجِعَ» (سنن بيهقي: باب من قال عزم الطلاق انقضاء الأربعة الأشهر، نمبر 15231)
اصول: ایلاء: شوہر چار ماہ تک بیوی سے نہ ملنے کی قسم کھائے، بایں صورت اگر شوہر ان ایام میں نہ ملے تو ایک طلاق بائنہ ہو جائے گی، اور اگر اس مدت سے قبل ملاقات کر لیا تو ایلاء ختم ہو گا اور قسم کا کفارہ لازم ہو گا۔
Book of Ila'. He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: When a husband says to his wife, 'By Allah, I will not approach you' or 'By Allah, I will not approach you for four months,' then he is a muli (one who makes ila'). If he has intercourse with her within the four months, he breaks his oath, and the kaffarah becomes obligatory upon him, and the ila' falls. Proof (1): The verse for establishing when the husband says... (Surah al-Baqarah 2:226-227). Proof (2): The hadith for establishing when the husband says... Anas ibn Malik heard: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) made ila' from his wives and his foot was dislocated, so he stayed in his room for twenty-nine days, then came down, and they said, 'O Messenger of Allah, you made ila' for a month?' He said: 'The month is twenty-nine.' (Bukhari). Proof (3): The saying of the Companion for establishing when the husband says... Ibn Abbas said: 'There is no ila' except with an oath' (Ibn Abi Shaybah). And for the ruling that if he has intercourse within the four months, that is the expiation of your oaths when you swear... (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:89). And proof (2) for the ruling that if he has intercourse within the four months: 'For those who swear off their wives, a waiting of four months; if they return, then Allah is Forgiving, Merciful' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:226). And proof (3) for the ruling that if he has intercourse within the four months: Ibn Abbas said: 'The man swears by Allah not to have intercourse with his wife; she waits four months; if he has intercourse, he must expiate by feeding ten poor people or clothing them or freeing a slave; if he cannot, then fasting three days. If four months pass before he has intercourse, the Sultan gives him the choice: either to return (fa'ah) and take back his wife...' (Bayhaqi). Principle: Ila': The husband swears not to have intercourse with his wife for four months. In this case, if the husband does not have intercourse during these days, one ba'in divorce will occur. And if he meets (i.e., has intercourse) before this period, the ila' ends and the kaffarah of the oath becomes obligatory.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Ila' defines ila' (an oath of abstinence from marital relations) and its legal consequences. The matn states that if a husband swears by Allah not to approach his wife for a period of four months or more, he becomes a muli. If he breaks his oath by having intercourse within the four months, he has violated his oath and must pay the standard kaffarah for breaking an oath (expiation: feeding ten poor, clothing them, or freeing a slave; if unable, fasting three days), and the ila' is cancelled. If the four months pass without intercourse, the court gives him a choice: either to return (fi'ah) to his wife (meaning to resume marital relations) or to divorce her. If he refuses both, the judge can enforce a divorce. The passage then provides three proofs for the definition: the Quranic verse (2:226-227) which mentions the waiting period of four months for those who make ila' and the options of return or divorce; the hadith of the Prophet's own ila' showing that it is a valid and recognized practice; and the saying of Ibn Abbas that ila' is only valid with an oath. For the requirement of kaffarah upon breaking the oath, it cites another verse (5:89) on expiation of oaths, the same verse (2:226) implying that if he returns he must expiate, and Ibn Abbas's explicit statement on the expiation. The Urdu summary clarifies the Hanafi position: after four months without intercourse, one ba'in divorce occurs automatically; if he returns before four months, the ila' ends and kaffarah is due. Note that the initial matn only mentions the case of breaking the oath, but the commentary adds the consequence of four months passing.

Key Terms
إيلاء (īlā'): An oath taken by a husband to abstain from sexual relations with his wife for a period of four months or more.
مولٍ (mūlin): A husband who has made ila' (taken an oath of abstinence).
فيء (fay'): Returning to marital relations; breaking the oath of ila' by having intercourse within the four-month period.
الكفارة (al-kaffārah): Expiation for breaking an oath: feeding ten poor, clothing them, or freeing a slave; if unable, fasting three days.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the matn of Quduri, what happens if a husband who has made ila' has intercourse with his wife within the four-month period?
A) He is considered to have divorced her.
B) The ila' continues and no kaffarah is required.
C) He has broken his oath, must pay kaffarah, and the ila' is cancelled.
D) The period is extended by another four months.

Key Takeaway
Ila' is a valid oath of abstinence that either requires kaffarah upon return or triggers a ba'in divorce after four months without return.

Ila': Definition and Ruling on Return
Defines ila' and states ruling for return within four months.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of ila' in Hanafi fiqh and apply the ruling when the husband returns within four months.

Core Idea
Ila' is an oath to abstain for at least four months; returning within four months breaks the oath and requires kaffarah.

This foundational passage from Al-Quduri defines the concept of ila' and outlines the first of two possible outcomes: the husband's return (fay'ah) within the waiting period. Understanding this ruling is essential for grasping the larger framework of divorce-related obligations in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is ila' (a husband's oath to abstain from intercourse for four months or more). The ruling: if he returns (has intercourse) within the four months, he breaks his oath and must pay kaffarah (expiation). The ila' then drops.
The kaffarah for a broken oath is feeding ten poor people, clothing them, freeing a slave, or fasting three days.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is Quran 2:226-227, which mentions the waiting period of four months and the two outcomes: return (fay'ah) or resolve for divorce. Additional proofs include the hadith of Anas about the Prophet's ila' and the saying of Ibn Abbas that ila' requires an oath.
The hadith and Ibn Abbas' statement are supplementary proofs confirming the requirement of an oath.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Quranic verse uses 'yooloona' to indicate swearing (ila') and 'faa'u' for return. The term 'faa'u' implies actual intercourse, not a verbal statement. The ruling of kaffarah comes from the general rules of oath-breaking (Surah Al-Ma'idah 5:89).
The word 'tarabbus' (waiting period) indicates that the husband is given four months to decide.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْإِيلَاءِ
قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ - إِذَا قَالَ الزَّوْجُ لِامْرَأَتِهِ وَاللَّهِ لَا أَقْرَبُكِ أَوْ وَاللَّهِ لَا أَقْرَبُكِ أَرْبَعَةَ أَشْهُرٍ فَهُوَ مُولٍ. فَإِنْ وَطِئَهَا فِي الْأَرْبَعَةِ الْأَشْهُرِ حَنِثَ فِي يَمِينِهِ وَلَزِمَتْهُ الْكَفَّارَةُ وَسَقَطَ الْإِيلَاءُ.
وَدَلِيلُهُ قَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى: {لِلَّذِينَ يُؤْلُونَ مِن نِّسَائِهِمْ تَرَبُّصُ أَرْبَعَةِ أَشْهُرٍ فَإِن فَاءُوا فَإِنَّ اللَّهَ غَفُورٌ رَّحِيمٌ} [البقرة:226]، وَقَوْلُهُ: {وَإِنْ عَزَمُوا الطَّلَاقَ فَإِنَّ اللَّهَ سَمِيعٌ عَلِيمٌ} [البقرة:227]، وَحَدِيثُ أَنَسٍ: «آلَى رَسُولُ اللَّهِ مِنْ نِسَائِهِ...»، وَقَوْلُ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ: «لَا إِيلَاءَ إِلَّا بِحَلِفٍ».
Book of Ila'. He (the author) said - may Allah have mercy on him - When the husband says to his wife: 'By Allah, I will not approach you' or 'By Allah, I will not approach you for four months', then he is a Mu'li. Then if he has intercourse with her within the four months, he breaks his oath and the expiation becomes due upon him, and the ila' drops. And its proof is His statement the Exalted: {For those who swear to abstain from their wives, a waiting period of four months; if they return, then Allah is Forgiving, Merciful} [Al-Baqarah 2:226], and His statement: {And if they resolve on divorce, then Allah is All-Hearing, All-Knowing} [Al-Baqarah 2:227], and the hadith of Anas: 'The Messenger of Allah swore abstinence from his wives...', and the saying of Ibn Abbas: 'There is no ila' except with an oath'.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri introduces the chapter on Ila'. Ila' is when a husband swears by Allah that he will not have sexual intercourse with his wife. The minimum period for it to be considered ila' is four months. If he swears for exactly four months or more, it is ila'. The first ruling is about the scenario where the husband returns to his wife within the four-month period. 'Fay'ah' means returning to normal marital relations. If he does so, he has broken his oath and must pay kaffarah (expiation) for breaking an oath, which is feeding or clothing ten poor people, or freeing a slave, or fasting three days. The ila' is then annulled and no further consequences follow. The author provides proofs: the Quranic verses from Surah Al-Baqarah which establish the concept of ila' and its two possible outcomes (return or divorce), the hadith from Anas showing the Prophet's own ila' as a precedent, and the statement of Ibn Abbas confirming that ila' requires an oath.

Key Terms
الإيلاء (al-īlā'): A husband's oath to abstain from sexual relations with his wife for a period of four months or more.
مولٍ (mūlin): The husband who has taken an oath of ila'.
فيئة (fay'ah): The husband's return to normal marital relations by having intercourse within the four-month period, thereby breaking his oath.
كفارة (kaffārah): The expiation required for breaking an oath, which in this context is feeding/clothing ten poor people, freeing a slave, or fasting three days.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He has committed ila' and the marriage is dissolved.
B) He has broken his oath; he must pay kaffarah and the ila' is annulled.
C) He is excused because he returned within four months.
D) He must divorce his wife.

Key Takeaway
Ila' is a valid oath of at least four months; returning within that period breaks the oath and requires kaffarah.

Automatic Talaq Ba'in in Ila' After Four Months
Explains automatic talaq ba'in after four months in ila' and sub-rulings on the oath.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the automatic occurrence of talaq ba'in upon expiry of four months in ila' and explain the sub-rulings regarding the oath.

Core Idea
In ila', the mere passage of four months without intercourse automatically triggers one irrevocable divorce (talaq ba'in) — no court order needed.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on ila' (vow of abstinence). When a husband swears not to approach his wife for four months or more, and the period expires without intercourse, the Hanafi school holds that the wife becomes irrevocably divorced by a single talaq. The ruling includes important distinctions about the oath's duration and its implications for remarriage and future divorces.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
State what happens when four months pass without intercourse in ila'.
2
Distinguish between oath durations
Explain the difference if the husband swore for only four months vs. forever.
3
Trace the consequences of remarriage
Describe what happens if the husband remarries the same wife after the first talaq ba'in, especially regarding the oath and potential further divorces.
4
Analyze the effect of an intervening marriage
Understand why a marriage to a second husband nullifies the original ila' for future divorces but not the oath.
5
Examine the proof
Identify the dalil (companion statements) and understand why it supports the Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ لَمْ يَقْرَبْهَا حَتَّى مَضَتْ أَرْبَعَةُ أَشْهُرٍ بَانَتْ مِنْهُ بِتَطْلِيقَةٍ. فَإِنْ كَانَ حَلَفَ عَلَى أَرْبَعَةِ أَشْهُرٍ فَقَطْ سَقَطَتِ الْيَمِينُ. وَإِنْ حَلَفَ عَلَى الْأَبَدِ فَالْيَمِينُ بَاقِيَةٌ، فَإِنْ عَادَ فَتَزَوَّجَهَا عَادَ الْإِيلَاءُ، فَإِنْ وَطِئَهَا وَإِلَّا وَقَعَتْ عِنْدَ مُضِيِّ أَرْبَعَةِ أَشْهُرٍ تَطْلِيقَةٌ أُخْرَى. فَإِنْ تَزَوَّجَهَا بَعْدَ زَوْجٍ لَمْ يَقَعْ بِذَلِكَ الْإِيلَاءِ طَلَاقٌ وَالْيَمِينُ بَاقِيَةٌ، فَإِنْ وَطِئَهَا كَفَّرَ عَنْ يَمِينِهِ.
وَدَلِيلُ هَذِهِ الْأَحْكَامِ مِمَّا رُوِيَ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، وَعُثْمَانَ، وَزَيْدِ بْنِ ثَابِتٍ، وَإِبْرَاهِيمَ النَّخَعِيِّ.
And if he does not approach her until four months have passed, she becomes ba'in from him by one divorce. Then if he swore for only four months, the oath drops. And if he swore for eternity, the oath remains, so if he returns and marries her, the ila' returns; if he has intercourse with her and otherwise, upon the passage of four months another divorce occurs. Then if he marries her after (she has been with) a husband, no divorce occurs by that ila' and the oath remains; if he has intercourse with her, he expiates his oath. And the proof of these rulings is what has been narrated from Ibn Abbas, Uthman, Zayd ibn Thabit, and Ibrahim al-Nakha'i.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage covers the scenario where the four months of ila' elapse without the husband having intercourse. In the Hanafi school, the wife automatically becomes ba'in (irrevocably divorced) by a single talaq. The text then distinguishes two cases regarding the nature of the oath. If the husband only swore for four months, the oath ends because its term has expired. If he swore forever (i.e., not to approach her ever), the oath remains in force. Consequently, if they later remarry, a new ila' is contracted. If the husband again avoids intercourse for another four months, another talaq will occur. However, if the wife marries another man (second husband) in the interim, the original ila' does not cause a talaq in the new marriage; the oath remains, and if the husband (original) marries her again, he must pay kaffarah if he has intercourse. The proofs are from the statements of prominent companions and a follower, supporting the automatic occurrence of talaq.

Key Terms
بائنة (bā'inah): An irrevocable divorce (talaq ba'in) that severs the marriage immediately; the husband cannot take her back without a new marriage and her consent.
تطليقة (taṭlīqah): A single count of divorce (one talaq).
يمين (yamīn): The oath sworn by the husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what happens exactly when four months pass in an ila' without the husband having intercourse?
A) The marriage continues as if nothing happened.
B) The wife becomes ba'in with one talaq automatically.
C) The husband must be taken to court to obtain a divorce.
D) The husband's oath is nullified and he must pay kaffarah.

Key Takeaway
The automatic occurrence of one talaq ba'in upon expiry of four months in ila' is a distinctive Hanafi ruling, with the fate of the oath depending on its duration.

Rulings on Ila' (Vow of Abstinence) and the Dispute with Shafi'i
Establishes basic rulings of ila' and the dispute with Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ila' after four months and explain why the Shafi'i school differs.

Core Idea
Ila' causes automatic talaq after four months; the oath remains if eternal.

Ila' is a serious vow that has automatic consequences in Hanafi fiqh. The classical text of Al-Quduri presents the ruling and then provides evidence from the Companions. This lesson walks through the ruling, the proof, and the key dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is ila'? It is a vow to abstain from intercourse. The ruling: after four months without intercourse, one bain talaq occurs automatically.
The talaq is bain (irrevocable minor divorce).
2
Locate the Hanafi dalil
The matn cites the saying of Ibn Abbas: 'When four months pass, she is one bain.' Similar reports from Uthman and Zayd ibn Thabit.
These are qawl al-sahabi proofs.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit phrase 'she is one bain' indicates that the divorce takes effect automatically without any action from the husband.
The imperative is not present; it is a declarative statement.
4
Note the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i argues based on Ibn Umar's report that the husband is stopped and made to divorce, not automatically divorced.
The Shafi'i school requires a court order.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on multiple Companions (Ibn Abbas, Uthman, Zayd) and considers their practice stronger. The mufta bihi is automatic talaq.
Ila' is a valid oath; the consequence is built into the vow.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْإِيلَاءِ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَقْرَبُهَا حَتَّى مَضَتْ أَرْبَعَةُ أَشْهُرٍ بَانَتْ مِنْهُ بِتَطْلِيقَةٍ فَإِنْ كَانَ حَلَفَ عَلَى أَرْبَعَةِ أَشْهُرٍ فَقَطْ سَقَطَتْ الْيَمِينُ. وَإِنْ حَلَفَ عَلَى الْأَبَدِ فَالْيَمِينُ بَاقِيَةٌ فَإِنْ عَادَ فَتَزَوَّجَهَا عَادَ الإِيلَاءُ فَإِنْ وَطِئَهَا وَإِلَّا وَقَعَتْ عِنْدَ مَضَى أَرْبَعَةِ أَشْهُرٍ تَطْلِيقَةٌ أُخْرَى فَإِنْ تَزَوَّجَهَا بَعْدَ زَوْجٍ لَمْ يَقَعْ بِذَلِكَ الْإِيلَاءِ طَلَاقٌ وَالْيَمِينُ بَاقِيَةٌ فَإِنْ وَطِئَهَا كَفَّرَ عَنْ يَمِينِهِ جُبَيْرٍ : أَكَانَ وَجْه (١) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَقْرَبْهَا حَتَّى مَضَتْ أَرْبَعَةُ أَشْهُرٍ: قُلْتُ لِسَعِيدِ بْنِ جُبَيْرٍ: أَكَانَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ يَقُولُ: «إِذَا مَضَتْ أَرْبَعَةُ أَشْهُرٍ فَهِيَ وَاحِدَةٌ بَائِنَةٌ وَلَا عِدَّةَ عَلَيْهَا وَتَزَوَّجْ إِنْ شَاءَتْ؟» قَالَ: نَعَمْ. (دَارُ قُطْنِي: ١٦ كِتَابُ الطَّلَاقِ وَالْخُلَعِ وَالْإِيلَاءِ، نَمْبَر ٤٠٤٨، سُنَنُ الْبَيْهَقِيِّ: بَابُ عَزْمِ الطَّلَاقِ انْقِضَاءُ الْأَرْبَعَةِ الْأَشْهُرِ، نَمْبَر ١٥٢٢٣، مُصَنَّفُ عَبْدِ الرَّزَّاقِ: بَابُ الْإِيلَاءِ، نَمْبَر ١١٦٠٥) وَجْه (٢) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَقْرَبْهَا حَتَّى مَضَتْ أَرْبَعَةُ أَشْهُرٍ: عَنْ عُثْمَانَ، وَزَيْدِ بْنِ ثَابِتٍ أَنَّهُمَا كَانَا يَقُولَانِ: «إِذَا مَضَتِ الْأَرْبَعَةُ أَشْهُرٍ فَهِيَ تَطْلِيقَةٌ بَائِنَةٌ». (دَارُ قُطْنِي: ١٦ كِتَابُ الطَّلَاقِ وَالْخُلَعِ وَالْإِيلَاءِ، نَمْبَر ٤٠٤٤، مُصَنَّفُ عَبْدِ الرَّزَّاقِ: بَابُ انْقِضَاءِ الْأَرْبَعَةِ، نَمْبَر ١١٦٣٩) وَجْه (١) دَلِيلُ الشَّافِعِيِّ: قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَقْرَبْهَا حَتَّى مَضَتْ أَرْبَعَةُ أَشْهُرٍ: عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ: إِذَا مَضَتْ أَرْبَعَةُ أَشْهُرٍ يُوقَفُ حَتَّى يُطَلَّقَ، وَلَا يَقَعُ عَلَيْهِ الطَّلَاقُ حَتَّى يُطَلَّقَ. وَيُذْكَرُ ذَلِكَ عَنْ عُثْمَانَ وَعَلِيٍّ وَأَبِي الدَّرْدَاءِ وَعَائِشَةَ وَاثْنَيْ عَشَرَ رَجُلًا مِنْ أَصْحَابِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم. (بُخَارِيُّ شَرِيفٌ: بَابُ قَوْلِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى لِلَّذِينَ يُؤْلُونَ مِن نِّسَآئِهِمْ تَرَبُّصُ أَرْبَعَةِ أَشْهُرٍ، نَمْبَر ٥٢٩١) ه وَجْه (١) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَإِنْ حَلَفَ عَلَى الْأَبَدِ فَالْيَمِينُ بَاقِيَةٌ: عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ قَالَ: «إِذَا مَضَتِ الْأَشْهُرُ فَقَدْ بَانَتْ مِنْهُ، فَإِنْ تَزَوَّجَهَا بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ فَهُوَ مُولٍ أَيْضًا، وَإِنْ لَمْ يَمَسَّهَا حَتَّى تَقْضِيَ الْأَشْهُرُ فَقَدْ بَانَتْ مِنْهُ، وَإِنْ تَزَوَّجَهَا بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ فَهُوَ مُولٍ أَيْضًا، وَإِنْ لَمْ يَمَسَّهَا حَتَّى تَقْضِيَ الْأَشْهُرُ بَانَتْ مِنْهُ أَيْضًا». (مُصَنَّفُ عَبْدِ الرَّزَّاقِ: بَابُ الَّذِي يَحْلِفُ بِالطَّلَاقِ ثَلَاثًا أَنْ لَا يَقْرَبَهَا هَلْ يَكُونُ إِيلَاءً، ١١٦٣٦) أُصُول: اگر ایلاء میں ابدی قسم کھائی ہمیشہ کے لئے تو زندگی میں جب بھی صحبت کرے گا کفارہ لازم ہو گا۔
Book of Ila'. And if he does not approach her until four months pass, she becomes separated from him by one talaq. If he swore for exactly four months, the oath is absolved. And if he swore for eternity, the oath remains. Then if he returns and marries her, the ila' returns. If he has intercourse with her, otherwise there occurs after the passage of four months another talaq. Then if he marries her after a husband, no talaq occurs by that ila', and the oath remains. If he has intercourse with her, he must expiate for his oath. Jubayr: Did he? (1) The saying of the Companion to establish 'and if he does not approach her until four months pass': I said to Sa'id ibn Jubayr: 'Did Ibn Abbas say: When four months pass, she is one bain, no 'iddah upon her, and she may marry if she wishes?' He said: 'Yes.' (2) The saying of the Companion to establish 'and if he does not approach her until four months pass': From Uthman and Zayd ibn Thabit that they used to say: 'When the four months pass, then it is one bain talaq.' (1) The proof of al-Shafi'i: the saying of the Companion to establish 'and if he does not approach her until four months pass': From Ibn Umar: 'When four months pass, he is stopped until he divorces, and talaq does not occur upon him until he divorces.' And that is mentioned from Uthman, Ali, Abu al-Darda, Aisha, and twelve men from the Companions of the Prophet. Then (1) The saying of the Tabi'i to establish 'and if he swore for eternity, the oath remains': From Ibrahim: 'When the months pass, she has separated from him. Then if he marries her after that, he is a mooli again. If he does not touch her until the months pass, she separates from him. If he marries her after that, he is a mooli again. If he does not touch her until the months pass, she separates from him again.' Principle: If in ila' an eternal oath is taken, then forever whenever he has intercourse, expiation becomes obligatory.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proofs from matn Quduri on the book of Ila'. The matn states the core ruling: if a husband makes a vow of abstinence (ila') and does not have intercourse with his wife for four months, she becomes irrevocably divorced by one bain talaq. If he only swore for exactly four months, the oath expires. If he swore for eternity, the oath remains. If he remarries her after the divorce, the ila' returns; if he does not have intercourse, another talaq occurs after four months. If she marries another husband and then returns to him, the previous ila' does not cause a talaq, but the oath remains—if he has intercourse, he must expiate. The commentary then provides proofs: the saying of Ibn Abbas, Uthman, and Zayd ibn Thabit that automatic talaq occurs after four months. It then presents the Shafi'i proof from Ibn Umar and others that the husband must be made to divorce and talaq does not occur automatically. This is an inter-madhhab dispute. The Hanafi response is implicit in the preceding proofs. The commentary also gives a proof from Ibrahim for the ruling that the oath remains if sworn for eternity. The Urdu principle states that with an eternal oath, expiation is necessary whenever intercourse occurs.

Key Terms
الإيلاء (al-īlā'): A vow (yamīn) to abstain from sexual intercourse with one's wife for a period of four months or more.
بانت (bānat): She becomes separated (divorced) irrevocably (bainunah sughra).
اليمين باقية (al-yamīn bāqiyah): The oath remains in effect even after the talaq occurs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens when a husband who made ila' with an eternal oath does not have intercourse for four months?
A) The marriage is annulled with immediate effect.
B) One bain talaq occurs automatically, and the oath remains.
C) The husband is imprisoned until he divorces.
D) The wife must seek judicial dissolution.

Key Takeaway
Ila' automatically ends the marriage with one bain talaq after four months, and if the oath was eternal, it continues to require expiation upon intercourse.

Fi'ah When Distance Prevents Physical Contact
Ruling on fi'ah via tongue when distance prevents physical return

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on fi'ah when distance prevents access and apply the condition of ability to determine whether verbal or physical fi'ah is required.

Core Idea
When distance prevents consummation in ila', a word suffices; when ability returns, only intercourse fulfills the oath.

In the Hanafi school, ila' requires the husband to return to his wife (fi'ah) within four months, normally by intercourse. But what if he is physically unable to reach her? This passage from al-Quduri provides the exception: verbal declaration suffices. However, if his situation changes and he becomes able, the verbal fi'ah is voided and intercourse becomes obligatory again. Understanding this conditional rule prevents misapplication in real-life cases of separation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligation after ila'
After swearing ila', the husband must perform fi'ah (return) within four months. Normal fi'ah is intercourse.
This is the default ruling.
2
Recognize the exception for distance
If a distance prevents physical access throughout the ila' period, the requirement shifts from intercourse to a verbal statement.
The distance must be such that he cannot reach her at all within the period.
3
Understand the substitute: verbal fi'ah
The husband says 'fitu ilayha' (I have returned to her) or similar. Once uttered, the ila' is lifted.
The statement must be clear and explicit.
4
Note the contingency: return of ability
If before the period ends, the husband becomes able to reach his wife (e.g., distance removed), the verbal fi'ah becomes void.
Ability cancels the concession; intercourse now becomes the only valid fi'ah.
5
Apply the ruling to scenarios
Given a scenario, determine whether verbal fi'ah is acceptable or intercourse is required based on the husband's ability to physically reach his wife within the ila' period.
Key factor: can he actually have intercourse before the period ends?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْإِيلَاءِ
أَوْ كَانَ بَيْنَهُمَا مَسَافَةٌ لَا يَقْدِرُ أَنْ يَصِلَ إِلَيْهَا فِي مُدَّةِ الْإِيلَاءِ فَفَيْؤُهُ أَنْ يَقُولَ بِلِسَانِهِ فِتْت إِلَيْهَا فَإِذَا قَالَ ذَلِكَ سَقَطَ الْإِيلَاءُ الْوَإِنْ صَحَ فِي الْمُدَّةِ بَطَلَ ذَلِكَ الْفَيْءُ وَصَارَ فَيْؤُهُ الْحِمَاعَ
Book of Ila'. Or if there is between them a distance such that he cannot reach her within the period of ila', then his fi'ah is that he says with his tongue 'I have returned to her'. When he says that, the ila' falls. And if he becomes able (to reach her) within the period, that fi'ah becomes void and his fi'ah becomes intercourse.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling for a husband who has sworn ila' (an oath to abstain from intercourse for four months) but is physically separated from his wife by a distance that prevents him from reaching her within the ila' period. In such a case, the normal requirement of returning via actual intercourse is waived. Instead, he can perform fi'ah by merely stating with his tongue that he has returned to her. Once he utters these words, the ila' is lifted and no further obligation remains. However, if later within the ila' period the distance is removed and he becomes able to reach her, then his verbal fi'ah becomes nullified, and he must now actually have intercourse to maintain the fi'ah. This shows that verbal fi'ah is only a concession for those who are unable to physically consummate; if ability returns, the original ruling applies.

Key Terms
الْإِيلَاءُ (al-īlā'): An oath taken by a husband to abstain from sexual intercourse with his wife for four months or more.
الْفَيْءُ (al-fay'): The act of returning to the wife by resuming sexual relations; or, in cases of inability, a verbal declaration of return.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A husband swears ila' and then moves to another country. He cannot travel back within four months due to a broken leg. Which of the following is correct?
A) He must have intercourse somehow; distance is not an excuse.
B) He can say 'I have returned to you' over the phone and that counts as fi'ah.
C) He must wait until he recovers and then perform fi'ah by intercourse within the remaining time.
D) He must divorce immediately.

Key Takeaway
Fi'ah in ila' requires actual intercourse unless distance prevents; then verbal statement suffices, but if ability returns, physical intercourse becomes obligatory.

The Ruling on 'Anti 'Alayya Haram' and the Role of Intention
Legal effects of an ambiguous declaration based on intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four possible legal effects of saying 'Anti 'alayya haram' and explain how the husband's intention determines which effect applies.

Core Idea
Intention converts an ambiguous phrase into divorce, zihar, an oath, or nothing—only the husband's niyyah decides.

The declaration 'You are unlawful to me' is a classic example of kinayah (allusive speech) in Hanafi fiqh. Because the words are not explicit, the husband's intention becomes the decisive factor in determining the legal outcome. This passage from al-Quduri systematically lists the four possibilities and the evidence from the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The husband says 'Anti 'alayya haram' to his wife. This is an ambiguous statement, not explicitly divorce, zihar, or an oath.
Kinayah (allusive speech) requires investigation of intent.
2
Recognize the need for intention
The husband is asked about his intention (niyyah). The legal effect hinges on what he meant.
If he refuses, the default ruling applies (see step 5).
3
Examine the four possible intentions
The text lists: lying, divorce, zihar, or tahrim/prohibition with no specific intent.
Each leads to a distinct ruling.
4
Derive the ruling for each intention
Lying: no effect. Divorce: one talaq ba'in (unless three intended). Zihar: rules of zihar apply. Tahrim/no intent: it is an oath, making him one who has made ila'.
Talaq ba'in is irrevocable; zihar requires expiation; oath leads to ila'.
5
Connect to the proof
The Quranic verse (Surah al-Tahrim 66:1-2) treats making halal as haram as an oath, supporting the last ruling.
The verse provides the basis for treating tahrim as a yamin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا قَالَ لِامْرَأَتِهِ أَنْتِ عَلَيَّ حَرَامٌ سُئِلَ عَنْ نِيَّتِهِ فَإِنْ قَالَ أَرَدْت الْكَذِبَ فَهُوَ كَمَا قَالَ وَإِنْ قَالَ نَوَيْتِ الطَّلَاقَ فَهِيَ تَطْلِيقَةٌ بَائِنَةٌ إِلَّا أَنْ يَنْوِيَ الثَّلَاثَ وَإِنْ قَالَ أَرَدْت الظُّهَارَ فَهُوَ ظِهَارٌ وَإِنْ قَالَ أَرَدْت التَّحْرِيمَ أَوْ لَمْ أُرِدْ بِهِ شَيْئًا فَهُوَ يَمِينٌ يَصِيرُ بِمَا مُولِيَا
And when he says to his wife 'You are unlawful to me', he is asked about his intention. So if he says 'I intended lying', then it is as he said (i.e., nothing occurs). And if he says 'I intended divorce', then it is one irrevocable divorce (talaq ba'in) unless he intended three. And if he says 'I intended zihar', then it is zihar. And if he says 'I intended prohibition (tahrim)' or 'I did not intend anything by it', then it is an oath and he becomes thereby one who has made ila'.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage explains the Hanafi ruling on the ambiguous declaration 'You are unlawful to me.' Since this phrase is kinayah (allusive) – not explicitly divorce, zihar, or oath – the husband's intention determines the legal outcome. If he admits he was lying, no effect occurs. If he intended divorce, it results in one talaq ba'in (irrevocable divorce), unless he intended three, then three occur. If he intended zihar (likening his wife to his mother or a mahram), then the rules of zihar apply, requiring expiation before intercourse. If he intended merely to make her unlawful (tahrim) without divorce or zihar, or if he had no specific intention, it is treated as a普通的 oath (yamin), making him a person who has entered ila' – an oath to abstain from intercourse. The text then proceeds to provide evidence from Quran and hadith. The passage is foundational for understanding how kinayah words operate in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
الظِّهَارُ (az-zihar): A husband's statement likening his wife to a prohibited relative (e.g., 'you are like my mother's back'), requiring expiation before intercourse.
تَطْلِيقَةٌ بَائِنَةٌ (tatliqah ba'inah): An irrevocable divorce that ends the marriage immediately; the husband cannot take back his wife without a new marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A husband tells his wife 'You are unlawful to me' and later says he intended only to emphasize that she is like a forbidden relative. What is the ruling?
A) It is one talaq ba'in.
B) It is zihar.
C) It is an oath requiring no expiation.
D) It is nothing because he was lying.

Key Takeaway
The legal effect of an ambiguous divorce-related statement depends entirely on the husband's declared intention under oath.

Three Proofs that 'Haram' is an Oath
Quranic and hadith proofs for treating the phrase as an oath

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three textual evidences (Quran, Ibn Abbas, Ibn Mas'ud) for the Hanafi ruling that saying 'you are unlawful to me' without divorce or zihar intention constitutes an oath requiring expiation, and explain how each proof establishes the ruling.

Core Idea
The Quran and Companion sayings: declaring one's wife 'haram' without divorce or zihar intention is an oath, not a divorce.

The previous lesson established the ruling: a husband who says 'anti 'alayya haram' without intending divorce or zihar enters an oath (ila') and becomes a muli. This lesson presents the textual proofs — the Quranic verse from Surah at-Tahrim and the sayings of two Companions — that form the foundation of the Hanafi position. Understanding these proofs is key to appreciating the school's reliance on the Quran, hadith, and qawl al-sahabi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three proofs
The passage explicitly lists three 'wajh' (evidences): (1) a Quranic verse, (2) a saying of Ibn Abbas, (3) a saying of Ibn Mas'ud. First, note each source.
The editor uses 'وجه' to mark each proof.
2
Analyze the Quranic proof
Read Surah at-Tahrim 66:1-2. The verse rebukes the Prophet for prohibiting what Allah made lawful and states that Allah has ordained 'tahillat aymanikum' (dissolution of oaths). The Hanafi deduction: when a person declares something halal as haram, it falls under the category of oaths, not divorce or zihar. The word 'tahillah' implies expiation (kaffarah).
The verse is general; the Hanafis apply it to anyone, not just the Prophet.
3
Analyze the Companion sayings
Ibn Abbas said: 'Concerning (the word) haram, expiation is required.' Ibn Mas'ud stated: 'His intention matters; if he did not intend divorce, it is an oath.' Both sayings treat 'haram' as an oath requiring kaffarah. In Hanafi usul, qawl al-sahabi is a valid source of law when no other text contradicts.
These sayings are mawquf (stopped at Companion) but accepted as authoritative.
4
Connect proofs to the ruling
Together, the proofs establish that 'anti 'alayya haram' without divorce or zihar intention is an oath. The husband must perform kaffarah if he breaks the oath (by resuming intercourse). He becomes a muli (one who has entered ila'), with a waiting period of four months.
The evidence is consistent across the three sources.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَجْهُ (۱) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ وَإِنْ قَالَ أَرَدْتُ التَّحْرِيمَ يَا أَيُّهَا النَّبِيُّ لِمَ تُحَرِّمُ مَا أَحَلَّ اللَّهُ لَكَ تَبْتَغِي مَرْضَاتَ أَزْوَاجِكَ وَاللَّهُ غَفُورٌ رَّحِيمٌ قَدْ فَرَضَ اللَّهُ لَكُمْ تَحِلَّةَ أَيْمَنِكُمْ سورة التحريم 66:1/2 وَجْهُ (۲) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ إِنَّ ابْنَ عَبَّاسٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا قَالَ «فِي الْحَرَامِ يُكَفَّرُ» (بخاري:4911، مسلم:1473) وَجْهُ (۳) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ عَنِ ابْنِ مَسْعُودٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ أَنَّهُ كَانَ يَقُولُ: نِيَّتُهُ فِي الْحَرَامِ مَا نَوَى إِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ نَوَى طَلَاقًا فَهِيَ يَمِينٌ
Evidence (1): The verse to establish that if he says 'I intended prohibition': 'O Prophet, why do you prohibit what Allah has made lawful to you, seeking the approval of your wives? And Allah is Forgiving and Merciful. Indeed, Allah has ordained for you the dissolution of your oaths.' (Surah at-Tahrim 66:1-2). Evidence (2): The saying of the Companion to establish that Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with him, said: 'Concerning (the word) 'haram', expiation is required.' Evidence (3): The saying of the Companion to establish that Ibn Mas'ud, may Allah be pleased with him, used to say: 'His intention matters in 'haram'; if he did not intend divorce, then it is an oath.'
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage provides the textual evidence for the ruling in the previous lesson. The Hanafi school uses three proofs. First, the Quranic verse from Surah at-Tahrim, which tells the Prophet (peace be upon him) that making something halal haram requires expiation of an oath. This shows the general principle that declaring something haram (even one's wife) is an oath, not divorce. Second, the statement of Ibn Abbas (a Companion) that 'haram' requires kaffarah (expiation). Third, the statement of Ibn Mas'ud (another Companion) that intention is key; if no divorce is intended, it is an oath. These are cited as 'qawl al-sahabi' (saying of a Companion), which in Hanafi usul is a valid source of law. Together, they solidify the ruling that saying 'you are unlawful to me' without divorce or zihar intention results in an oath, making the husband a person in ila'.

Key Terms
التَّحِلَّةُ (at-tahillah): The dissolution or expiation of an oath (kaffarah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses the Quran and Companion sayings to prove that saying 'you are unlawful to me' without divorce or zihar intention is an oath, not a divorce, requiring expiation if broken.

Ruling on Taking Extra from a Nashiz Wife in Khul'
Ruling on husband taking extra in khul' with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the husband taking more than the dowry when the wife is nashiz and identify the hadith proof.

Core Idea
Taking more than the dowry in khul' is disliked but valid – the prohibition is moral, not legal.

In khul', the wife compensates the husband to end the marriage. But what if she is the one at fault? Al-Quduri clarifies: the husband should not take more than he gave, but if he does, the divorce still stands. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof from the Prophet's ﷺ instruction to Jamila's husband, and why the Hanafi school treats it as dislike rather than prohibition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the husband taking more than the original dowry from a nashiz wife in khul'. The ruling is 'yukrah' (disliked) but 'jaza fi al-qada' (valid judicially). Thus it is makruh tanzihi, not haram.
Makruh tanzihi means disliked but not sinful enough to invalidate the contract.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Jamila bint Salul. She came to the Prophet ﷺ and said she could not bear her husband due to hatred. The Prophet asked if she would return the garden (dowry). She agreed. The Prophet ordered the husband to take the garden and not increase.
The hadith is ahad (single chain), giving zanni thubut and dalala.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'wa la yazdad' (and do not increase) is an explicit prohibition. However, the Hanafi school interprets it as a moral counsel (irshad) rather than a legal commands (wujub). The reason: the context of Jamila's nushuz was specific, and the husband's right to compensation is recognized.
This is why taking extra is not invalid – the prohibition is not absolute.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school (and some others) consider taking extra to be haram and may even render the khul' invalid. They take the hadith's prohibition at face value.
The practical effect: in Shafi'i, the husband cannot take extra; if he does, the khul' is fasid or batil.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position (makruh tanzihi, valid) is based on the principle that khul' is an exchange contract, and the wife's nushuz does not cancel the husband's right to compensation. The hadith is taken as guidance to avoid taking more, but not as a nullifier.
The mufta bihi ruling is as in the matn: disliked but valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ كَانَ النُّشُوزُ مِنْ قِبَلِهَا كُرِهَ لَهُ أَنْ يَأْخُذَ مِنْهَا أَكْثَرَ مِمَّا أَعْطَاهَا فَإِنْ فَعَلَ ذَلِكَ جَازَ فِي الْقَضَاءِ. عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، أَنَّ جَمِيلَةَ بِنْتَ سَلُولَ، أَتَتِ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَقَالَتْ : ٠٠٠٠لَا أُطِيقُهُ بُغْضًا، فَقَالَ لَهَا النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «أَتَرُدِّينَ عَلَيْهِ قَالَتْ: نَعَمْ، فَأَمَرَهُ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَنْ يَأْخُذَ مِنْهَا حَدِيقَتَهُ، وَلَا يَزْدَادَ
And if the nushuz (disobedience) is from her side, it is disliked for him to take from her more than what he gave her. If he does that, it is permitted judicially. From Ibn Abbas: that Jamila bint Salul came to the Prophet (saw) and said: '... I cannot bear him due to hatred.' The Prophet said to her: 'Will you return his garden to him?' She said: 'Yes.' So the Messenger of Allah ordered him to take his garden from her and not increase.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
Passage type: Ruling with proof. The text states the ruling: if the wife is the one committing nushuz (disobedience), it is makruh for the husband to take more than the dowry he gave her as compensation in khul'. However, if he does so, the khul' is valid and the extra amount is taken in judicial terms (meaning the judge will enforce it). The proof is the hadith of Jamila bint Salul, the famous story of the first khul' in Islam. The husband was given back exactly his garden, no more. This shows that taking extra is discouraged but not invalid.

Key Terms
نُشُوز (nushūz): Disobedience or recalcitrance of the wife towards her husband.
خُلْع (khulʿ): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation to the husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is haram and void.
B) It is disliked but valid.
C) It is recommended.
D) It is mandatory.

Key Takeaway
The husband may not take more than the dowry from a nashiz wife in khul' as a moral ideal, but if he does, the khul' remains valid and enforceable.

Ruling on Talaq with Compensation and Its Bain Effect
Ruling on divorce in exchange for compensation and its classification as bain

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a divorce in exchange for compensation is bain and identify the proof from the hadith.

Core Idea
A divorce for compensation (khul') is a bain talaq, not an annulment, and counts towards the three divorces.

When a couple cannot reconcile, Islamic law provides a mechanism for the wife to obtain a divorce by returning the mahr or paying compensation. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that such a divorce (khul') is irrevocable (bain) and counts as one of the three permissible divorces.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act is talaq in exchange for compensation (khul'). The ruling is that it is valid and results in a bain divorce.
The text says 'waqa'a al-talaq' and 'kana al-talaqu baina'.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? Two hadith from Ibn Abbas: one about ransom even with a headband, the other stating the Prophet made khul' a bain talaq.
The author quotes these as evidence.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How exactly does this dalil prove the ruling? The first hadith shows any property can be compensation; the second explicitly states khul' is a bain talaq, establishing it as a divorce and not an annulment.
The legal link is the direct statement of the Prophet.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Does any school disagree? Yes, the Shafi'i school considers khul' a faskh (annulment) rather than talaq, meaning it does not count towards the three divorces.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Which position is relied upon? The Hanafi position is mufta bihi, based on the explicit hadith. The ikhtilaf does not affect the operative ruling within the school.
The authority_weight is zahir_riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ طَلَّقَهَا عَلَى مَالِ فَقَبِلَتْ وَقَعَ الطَّلَاقُ وَلَرْمَهَا الْمَالُ وَكَانَ الطَّلَاقُ بَائِنَا. عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسِ تَختَلِعُ حَتَّى بِعِقَاصِهَا. عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ رضي الله عنهما أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم جَعَلَ الخُلْعَ تَطْلِيقَةً بَائِنَةً
And if he divorces her for a property, and she accepts, the divorce occurs and the property is binding on her, and the divorce is bain (irrevocable). From Ibn Abbas: 'She may redeem herself even to the extent of her headband.' From Ibn Abbas that the Prophet (saw) made khul' a bain (irrevocable) divorce.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
Passage type: Ruling with proof. The text states that when a husband divorces his wife for a compensation (mal) and she accepts, the divorce takes effect, the compensation becomes due from her, and the divorce is bain (irrevocable). This means the husband cannot take her back without a new marriage and new mahr. The proofs are two: 1) The narration from Ibn Abbas 'a woman may ransom herself even with her headband' indicating that any property acceptable as mahr can be used as compensation. 2) The hadith that the Prophet made khul' a bain divorce. This establishes the Hanafi position that khul' is a talaq and not a faskh.

Key Terms
بَائِن (bāʾin): An irrevocable divorce where the husband cannot take the wife back without a new marriage and mahr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Invalid Consideration in Khul' and Talaq
Ruling when consideration is invalid in khul' and talaq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when the consideration in khul' or talaq with compensation is invalid, and distinguish between the two scenarios.

Core Idea
Invalid consideration does not void divorce; khul' becomes bain, talaq becomes raj'i.

This passage from al-Quduri presents a concise ruling on two related scenarios: khul' and talaq with invalid consideration. The key insight is that the divorce itself remains valid, but its consequences (irrevocable vs. revocable) and the husband's right to compensation differ. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying Hanafi divorce law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
The passage covers two distinct situations: (1) khul' where the compensation (ʿiwaḍ) is something invalid in Islamic law (wine, pig, carrion), and (2) talaq with compensation where the consideration is invalid.
Khul' is initiated by the wife; talaq with compensation (like mubara'ah) is initiated by the husband.
2
Analyze the khul' ruling
In khul', if the consideration is invalid, the husband receives no compensation, but the divorce still takes effect as a bain (irrevocable) divorce. The separation is final.
The phrase 'fa lā shay'a lil-zawji wa al-furqatu bā'inatun' is the key.
3
Analyze the talaq ruling
In a talaq with compensation, if the consideration is invalid, the divorce remains valid but becomes rajʿī (revocable), meaning the husband can take her back during the ʿiddah without a new marriage.
This contrasts with khul': although both involve invalid consideration, the nature of the divorce differs.
4
Extract the general principle
The passage ends with a general principle: anything valid as mahr (dower) can be valid as substitute (badal) in khul'. This links back to the requirement that the consideration must be lawful property (māl mutaqawwim).
This principle is used to determine whether a given item can be consideration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ بَطَلَ الْعِوَضُ فِي الخُلْعِ مِثْلُ أَنْ يُخَالِعَ الْمُسْلِمَةَ عَلَى خَمْرٍ أَوْ خِنْزِيرٍ أَوْ مَيْتَةٍ فَلَا شَيْءَ لِلزَّوْجِ وَالْفُرْقَةُ بَائِنَةٌ وَإِنْ بَطَلَ الْعِوَضُ فِي الطَّلَاقِ كَانَ رَجْعِيًّا وَمَا جَازَ أَنْ يَكُون مَهْرًا جَازَ أَنْ يَكُون بَدَلًا في الخلع
And if the consideration in khul' is invalid, such as if he divorces a Muslim woman in exchange for wine, or pig, or carrion, then nothing is due to the husband and the separation is bain. And if the consideration in talaq (with compensation) is invalid, it becomes raj'i. And whatever is permitted as mahr is permitted as substitute in khul'.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
Passage type: Ruling statement. The text lays out two scenarios. First, in khul', if the compensation is something invalid in Islamic law (like wine, pig, carrion), the husband gets no compensation, but the divorce still takes effect as a bain (irrevocable) divorce. This is because the khul' itself is valid; only the compensation is corrupted. Second, in a talaq with compensation (like mubara'ah or talaq ala mal), if the consideration is invalid, it does not affect the validity of the divorce; however, the divorce becomes raj'i (revocable) instead of bain. The difference is because in khul', the wife's desire for separation is stronger, so the divorce is made bain regardless. Finally, any item valid as mahr can be used as substitute in khul' (i.e., it must be lawful and of value).

Key Terms
عِوَض (ʿiwaḍ): Compensation paid by the wife to the husband in exchange for divorce.
رَجْعِي (rajʿī): Revocable divorce during the 'iddah period; the husband can take her back without a new marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if a husband divorces his wife in khul' in exchange for wine (which is invalid consideration)?
A) The divorce is invalid and she remains his wife.
B) The divorce is bain and the husband gets nothing.
C) The divorce is raj'i and the husband gets the value of wine.
D) The husband gets the wine as compensation.

Key Takeaway
Invalid consideration in khul' yields a bain divorce with no compensation; in talaq with compensation, the divorce becomes raj'i.

Khul' Compensation for Unspecified Consideration
Three wordings of khul' with their compensation outcomes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the compensation due in khul' when the wife's consideration is unspecified, based on the wording used.

Core Idea
In khul', compensation depends on wording: absolute 'what I have' yields nothing; 'of property' yields mahr; 'dirhams' yields three dirhams.

Khul' is a divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation. The Hanafi school emphasizes that precise wording determines the outcome. This passage from al-Quduri presents three cases where the wife offers what she possesses but actually has nothing. The rulings illustrate how the law infers a default from the wording.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Three Wordings
Extract the three distinct phrases the wife uses: (1) 'ala ma fi yadi' (for what is in my hand), (2) 'ala ma fi yadi min mal' (for what is in my hand of property), (3) 'ala ma fi yadi min darahima' (for what is in my hand of dirhams).
The wording is the key variable.
2
Determine the Default Assumption for Each Wording
When the wife has nothing, the law presumes a default value based on the wording: (1) absolute wording → nothing is implied, (2) 'mal' (property) → the mahr (dower) is the default property in the marital context, (3) 'dirhams' → a standard minimal amount of three dirhams is presumed.
The default flows from the common understanding of the terms.
3
Derive the Compensation for Each Scenario
Apply the default to determine what the wife must pay: (1) Nothing – compensation is zero; (2) The full mahr – she returns what she received; (3) Three dirhams – she pays a fixed sum.
The khul' itself is valid in all three; only the compensation varies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا قَالَتْ لَهُ خَالِعْنِي عَلَى مَا فِي يَدِي فَخَالَعَهَا وَلَمْ يَكُنْ فِي يَدِهَا شَيْءٌ فَلَا شَيْءَ لَهُ عَلَيْهَا وَإِنْ قَالَتْ عَلَى مَا فِي يَدِي مِنْ مَالٍ فَخَالَعَهَا وَلَمْ يَكُنْ فِي يَدِهَا شَيْءٌ رَدَّتْ عَلَيْهِ مَهْرَهَا وَإِنْ قَالَتْ عَلَى مَا فِي يَدِي مِنْ دَرَاهِمَ أَوْ مِنْ الدَّرَاهِم فَفَعَلَ وَلَمْ يَكُنْ فِي يَدِهَا شَيْءٌ فَلَهُ عَلَيْهَا ثَلَاثَةُ دَرَاهِمَ
And if she says to him: 'Divorce me in khul' for what is in my hand,' and he divorces her and she has nothing in her hand, then nothing is due from her. And if she says: 'for what is in my hand of property,' and he divorces her and she has nothing, she must return the mahr to him. And if she says: 'for what is in my hand of dirhams or from dirhams,' and he does so and she has nothing, then he has three dirhams from her.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
Passage type: Ruling statement. The text presents three cases where a wife initiates khul' by referring to unspecified items in her hand, and it turns out she had nothing. The rulings depend on the wording: (1) If she says 'for what is in my hand' (absolute), he gets nothing because it was ambiguous. (2) If she says 'for what is in my hand of property' (mal, which may include the mahr), she must return the mahr she received because the default 'mal' in her hand could be understood as the mahr. (3) If she specifies 'dirhams' (a known currency), the default minimum is three dirhams (a recognized amount in Hanafi law). This shows the importance of precise wording in khul' contracts.

Key Terms
مَهْر (mahr): The obligatory bridal gift paid by husband to wife at marriage.
خلع (khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation paid to the husband.
درهم (dirham): A silver coin used as currency in classical Islamic law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a wife says 'khala'ni 'ala ma fi yadi min darahim' but she has nothing, how much must she pay?
A) Nothing
B) The mahr
C) Three dirhams
D) An amount to be determined by a judge

Key Takeaway
The precise wording in khul' determines the compensation when the offered property is absent.

Talaq — Divorce
beginner
6 min
Proportional Compensation in Talaq with Offer for Multiple Divorces
Ruling when wife offers three divorces for a thousand and receives one.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the proportional compensation due when a wife offers a lump sum for a specific number of divorces but the husband gives fewer.

Core Idea
Compensation for talaq is divisible: paying for three divorces but receiving one reduces the payment to one-third.

In Hanafi law, a wife may offer compensation to her husband in exchange for divorce (khul'). A common scenario is when she offers a fixed amount for a specific number of divorces. This lesson examines the ruling when the husband divorces her fewer times than she offered for. The principle is straightforward: the compensation is apportioned ratably.

Guided Path
1
Identify the wife's offer
The wife says 'Divorce me three times for a thousand.' Note the two elements: the number of divorces (3) and the compensation amount (1000 dirhams). This sets the scope of the agreement.
The offer is conditional: she ties the payment to the number of divorces.
2
Identify the husband's action
The husband divorces her once. He does not fulfill the full number of divorces she offered for. This triggers the need to apportion the compensation.
The husband has the right to give fewer divorces than offered, but then the compensation is adjusted.
3
Apply proportional division
The ruling states that she owes only one-third of the thousand (i.e., 333.33 dirhams). This is because she offered for three divorces but received only one. The compensation is divided by the ratio of divorces given to divorces offered.
The divorces are considered countable units, making division possible.
4
Derive the underlying principle
The principle is that when compensation is offered for a specified number of divorces, it is divisible. If the husband gives fewer, the wife pays proportionally less. This applies to any similar scenario with different numbers.
The same principle applies if the husband gives more? (Not covered, but logically the wife would owe more? This is beyond the text, but can be explored in practice tasks.)

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذْ قَالَتْ طَلْقِني ثَلَاثًا بِأَلْفِ فَطَلَّقَهَا وَاحِدَةً فَعَلَيْهَا ثُلُثُ الْأَلْفِ
And when she said: 'Divorce me three times for a thousand,' and he divorced her once, then one-third of the thousand is due from her.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
Passage type: Ruling statement. This case deals with the scenario where the wife offers a specific amount (1000 dirhams) for three divorces, but the husband only gives one divorce. The rule is that the compensation is divided proportionally: she owes one-third of the agreed amount because only one out of three envisaged divorces occurred. This is based on the principle that the compensation is divisible when the subject matter (number of divorces) is divisible.

Key Terms
طَلَاق (ṭalāq): Divorce; the dissolution of marriage by the husband's pronouncement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a wife offers 1000 dirhams for three divorces, but the husband divorces her only once, how much is she required to pay?
A) 1000 dirhams
B) Nothing
C) 333.33 dirhams (one-third)
D) 500 dirhams

Key Takeaway
When a wife offers a lump sum for a specific number of divorces and receives fewer, she owes only proportionally.
